Government Proposes Major Reforms to the Soviet Constitution Through the Congress 27

Seeking Greater Democratization of the Electoral System

Workers and Peasants Enjoy Equal Political Rights

Moscow – The Soviet Union has today become a democratic country, at least in theory, as the Soviet Congress has unanimously passed a resolution stipulating the following three points: (1) secret ballot; (2) direct election of parliamentarians; (3) workers and peasants enjoy equal voting rights. Senior government observers predict that universal suffrage may end terror and strongly assert that they do not want to exert excessive pressure on universal suffrage. This thorough reform was proposed to the Congress by the government itself. Chairman of the Congress, Molotov, representing the Central Committee of the Communist Party, proposed amending the constitution to complete the necessary reforms. International political scholars say that the impact of liberating elections cannot yet be predicted, but this reform will in no way hinder Stalin's power. (Guomin dispatch, 6th)

Moscow – The Congress of the Soviet Federal Republic today unanimously passed a major reform plan, which is the prelude to a major reform of the Russian Constitution. After the vote, Molotov, Chairman of the Council of People's Commissars, addressed the public, saying that the various advantages of the parliamentary system will be adopted into the Soviet system in the future. Now that the class system has been abolished, secret ballots can be adopted. In the future, local Soviets can directly elect representatives to join the All-Union Congress and the Central Executive Committee, and both workers and peasants will have the same political rights. He hopes that the goal of universal suffrage will be achieved soon. (Reuters dispatch, 6th)

Moscow – Molotov, Chairman of the Council of People's Commissars of the Soviet Union, today proposed to the Soviet Congress that some parts of the Soviet Constitution should be changed. After a short debate by the delegates of the Congress (Kosior and Goloded also participated in the debate), the following resolution was unanimously passed: "After Molotov reported the resolution of the February Standing Committee of the Central Committee of the Communist Party on certain changes to the Soviet Constitution, the Seventh Congress of Soviet Delegates discussed it and concluded that the proposal of the Central Committee of the Communist Party was completely correct and timely, and instructed as follows:

(1) The Soviet Constitution should be amended as follows: (A) In order to further democratize the electoral system, the previous incomplete, unequal, stratified, and recorded ballot elections should be changed to equal, direct, and secret ballot elections; (B) The socio-economic foundation of the Constitution should be based on the current class relations in the Soviet Union (the establishment of new socialist industries, the elimination of rich peasants, the complete victory of the collective farming system, and the recognition of socialist property as the foundation of Soviet society, etc.) for a more precise stipulation.

(2) It is recommended that the Central Executive Committee select personnel to organize a constitutional committee responsible for drafting constitutional amendments based on the above principles and submit them to the Congress of the Central Executive Committee of the Soviet Union for approval.

(3) The next Soviet election should be carried out under the new system. When the Congress passed this resolution, there was thunderous applause that shook the roof. (TASS dispatch, 7th)

Moscow – Molotov reported on the issue of constitutional amendments, saying: "The Central Committee of the Communist Party respectfully submits to the Congress of Soviet Delegates some questions about the amendment of the Soviet Constitution. The Central Committee's submission of this question was based on Stalin's suggestion (the crowd applauded). The submission of this question was due to the following reasons: First, since Lenin laid the foundation for the Soviet Constitution in 1918, the relationship between the class forces in the Soviet Union has greatly changed, especially after the principle of socialist property has won victory in urban and rural areas; Second, we are now able to thoroughly implement Soviet democracy and make corresponding changes to the electoral system. The Soviet Constitution was formed in 1923, at which time the drafting committee was chaired by Stalin. However, the situation in our country today, such as its socio-economic structure, as well as the cultural and political development of the working masses, is completely incomparable with that of 1923." (excerpt) "The Central Committee of the Party is now submitting the following questions to the Congress as necessary measures to further democratize the Soviet system: First, abolish the current indirect election law and implement direct elections for all Soviet organs (from village and town Soviets to the Central Executive Committee of the Soviet Union), because direct elections can enhance the prestige of Soviet organs and strengthen their connection with the working masses. The highest Soviet organs will rise to a higher level. Currently, more and more capitalist countries are abandoning direct elections, and they are using the method of appointing officials to replace elections, while the Soviet Union is replacing indirect elections with direct elections. We stipulate that voters have the right to withdraw their elected representatives from any organ, and non-party organizations and groups of workers can pre-select candidates. If so, our Soviet system will take another step forward in the development of Soviet democracy.

Molotov then discussed the adoption of equal elections, saying: "The Soviet Constitution stipulates that workers should have more privileges than peasants in elections. The adoption of this method was because at that time, the general peasants were still small property owners, and at the same time, the rich peasants' forces in the countryside were very strong. Since the drafting of the Soviet Constitution, the situation has changed dramatically. The masses of peasants have abandoned their small private farming and joined collective farms to engage in the construction of a new socialist life. The masses of peasants have followed the workers in joining the ranks of socialist builders. The difference between workers and peasants has been widened, and the difference in their voting rights should be abolished first. Our abolition of unequal elections and the adoption of equal elections for all working masses will surely make the unity between workers and peasants closer and stronger, so the strength of the Soviet state will also increase day by day, and we will also have more success on our way to a society without classes."

"As for changing recorded ballots to secret ballots, this is a serious test of the connection between the Soviet government organs and the broad masses of workers. What it shows is that the source of the Soviet government's strength lies in strengthening and actively participating in the entire national administration by the masses, and increasing the masses' control over the entire national organs (whether upper or lower). As the Soviet state continues to consolidate the Soviet system, it can now fully realize all the advantages of universal direct equal and secret elections based on the Soviet system. The Soviets, in the past and today, are the foundation of our country's system. Only in today's Soviet Union can the advantages of the parliamentary system be fully realized, that is, the election of representatives of state administrative organs by all workers (as required by the Soviet Constitution) in a direct, equal, and secret manner."

"If so, the Soviet system should continue to develop in the following form: the district Soviets directly elected in each district, combined with the Soviet parliaments directly elected in each constitutional republic, and the All-Union Soviet Parliament. "Whether our friends or enemies, when they compare the development paths of bourgeois countries and the Soviet Union, they will be able to draw their conclusions. When our party boldly unfolds its great banner of proletarian democracy, capitalist countries will have angry predictions and cries of surprise. Therefore, we will understand the above point, and at the same time, when our friends in the camp express their new strength and trust in communism, we will also understand this point, that the leaders of capitalist countries have also realized that today's capitalism can be said to be historically hopeless. Although they speak differently, they involve the same facts, even more frankly. For example, a certain important person said, "Capitalist production methods have become a thing of the past." Another person said, "The collapse of 1929 was the collapse of the entire system," and so on. However, it is not difficult for us to imagine that the leaders of bourgeois society cannot draw correct conclusions from the above. Because the entire bourgeoisie always regards the private property of the means of production as "sacred and inviolable." All the efforts of the bourgeoisie are to use the state apparatus to protect this property. Our country's development path is completely different from this. The Soviet regime is resolutely advancing on the path of eliminating all classes and eliminating the psychological remnants of capitalism in people's minds, and has repeatedly achieved victories. The state apparatus is in the hands of the working class, and they rely on it to build a socialist society without classes. In the past, the Soviet state has used various methods to serve the Soviet people. In the future, it will surely be able to use various methods to consolidate socialist property, improve the lives of workers and peasants, and if necessary, it will also be able to use all its strength to defend our country's borders and meet the foreign enemies head-on. The strength of the principles of the Soviet state is invincible because the basis of its development lies in the increasingly broad participation of the masses in Soviet socialist construction. The questions we are discussing about the Soviet Constitution today reflect the great progress of socialism. At the same time, after the necessary amendments to the Constitution, it will surely further strengthen the Soviet regime. This power is based on the activities, consciousness, and organization of the masses in building a new society." (At the end of Mr. Molotov's speech, the audience applauded thunderously, and then the whole audience cheered.) (TASS dispatch, 7th)

Abolition of the U.S. Consulate in Moscow 28

Result of Debt Negotiations Breaking Down

No Change in Diplomatic Relations

Washington – After the State Department solemnly stated that the US-Russian debt negotiations had broken down and there was no hope for large orders from Soviet Russia, it announced today a major reduction in staff at the Moscow Embassy. In addition to the reduction in staff at the embassy, the consulate in Moscow will also be abolished, and all consulate staff will be withdrawn. After the indefinite suspension of US-Russian debt negotiations, President Roosevelt today refused to express his opinion in order to determine the responsibility for destroying the negotiations. President Roosevelt also did not comment on the news that he had acknowledged Soviet Russia's debt during the visit of Soviet Foreign Minister Litvinov to the United States. The United States recognized Soviet Russia immediately after President Roosevelt and Litvinov negotiated. (Guomin dispatch, 6th)

It is generally believed that the debt negotiations between the United States and Russia have now failed, and the consulates are like a decoration, so the State Department is abolishing them. (Havas dispatch, 6th)

Setback in the Restoration of Belgian-Russian Relations 29

Belgian Parliament Supports Government's Position

Advocates of Recognition Will Try Again

Brussels – The House of Representatives today, by a vote of 87 to 73, rejected the motion to restore diplomatic relations with Russia. Therefore, the suggestions of more radical members of Congress, asking the government to establish further relations with Soviet Russia, have at least suffered a setback. But the leaders of the recognition of Soviet Russia faction declared that they will unite their forces, continue their efforts, and start the struggle again, because they firmly believe that restoring relations with Russia is of great benefit to Belgium. However, the conservatives led by the Catholic Party still insist on refusing to fully recognize Soviet Russia, unless Soviet Russia abandons its revolutionary work. In particular, Soviet Russia should abandon its anti-religious movement. (Guomin dispatch, 6th)

Brussels – The Belgian House of Representatives today, by a vote of 87 to 83, supported the government's attitude and rejected the proposal to restore diplomatic relations between Belgium and Russia. Before the vote, the Foreign Minister explained the government's attitude, saying that the cabinet still adheres to the position of not restoring formal relations with Soviet Russia. The government does not want to see Soviet Russia's propaganda machine set up in Brussels. Belgium did not vote on Soviet Russia's accession to the League of Nations because Belgium firmly believes that the Russian government has committed the crime of destroying Belgian industries. The government is now watching the evolution of Sovietism, but has not seen any reason to change its current attitude. (Reuters dispatch, 6th)

Japanese Naval Minister's Remarks Did Not Excite the United States 30

It is learned that from now on, no matter what kind of warships Japan builds, the United States will compete with it. (Guomin dispatch, 6th)

Tokyo – Naval Minister Osumi yesterday, in response to questions from Seiyukai's Nakajima Yatariji at the fourth subcommittee of the House of Representatives Budget Committee, replied that he can still catch up with the current second supplementary plan, but in the future, it will be necessary to build auxiliary ships. Japanese Budget Subcommittee Questions Relations with China 31

Defense Minister Hayashi's Reply

Buying the CER is a Profitable Investment

Foreign Minister Hirota Answers Questions from Members

Tokyo – The House of Representatives held a fourth subcommittee meeting on the budget on the afternoon of the 7th. Defense Minister Hayashi stated that the military also hopes for a satisfactory relationship with China. The question and answer situation at the subcommittee meeting is briefly described below:

Mr. Shiozuki Manabu asked:

Does the Defense Minister think that today's situation is an extraordinary period?

Defense Minister Hayashi replied:

Since the Manchurian Incident, our country has shouldered a major responsibility, and is in a serious period in terms of foreign affairs. Moreover, we must fully assist in the development of (Manchukuo) in the future. Therefore, our country's defense area has expanded, so we believe that it is in an extremely serious situation. In other respects, it is influenced by external economic ideas, and it is by no means any ordinary period. Therefore, I have observed the above intentions and firmly believe that it is an extraordinary period.

Mr. Shiozuki asked:

Does China want to carry out positive work?

Defense Minister Hayashi replied:

This is a diplomatic issue, but from the perspective of East Asian peace, the military feels that it is necessary for relations with China to proceed smoothly.

Mr. Shiozuki asked:

From the perspective of the Far East situation, can the defense budget be reduced to the present level or more?

Mr. Saito Takao once raised a question at the formal meeting, roughly saying that the military department often increases the defense budget, which makes the world regard Japan as a warlike country and deepens its concept. The Defense Minister did not give any answer to the above question. We take this opportunity to hope to reveal our beliefs.

Defense Minister Hayashi replied:

Mr. Saito's question was directed to the Prime Minister, so I did not answer it. It is inappropriate to be suspected of being a warlike country because of the increased defense budget. Therefore, the military department, in view of the heavy and great responsibility of national defense, has only made the minimum request in order to complete it. (Nikkan dispatch, 7th)

Tokyo – Foreign Minister Hirota today had the following question and answer with Toshio Hanada (Seiyukai) regarding the CER issue at the first subcommittee meeting of the House of Representatives:

(Hirota) The CER purchase and sale treaty will be signed in one month, and will take effect immediately after signing.

(Hanada) What is the basis for setting the road price at 140 million yuan?

(Hirota) It is a mutual assistance between the two sides, and there is no basis.

(Hanada) Once Russia receives the road price, is there any fear that it will use it for military preparations on the border?

(Hirota) Judging from the current situation in Russia, it is unlikely that this will happen.

(Hanada) (Manchukuo) has not been established for long. Is the purchase of the CER with such a huge sum of money a huge impact on the economy?

(Hirota) The CER can be said to be a profitable investment, so it is expected that there will be no loss. (Kalian dispatch, 7th)

Germany's Internal Attitude is Not Uniform on the Anglo-French Agreement in London 34

Hitler Cancels Appointments to Focus on Research

German Ambassador to France Returns to His Post with New Instructions

Berlin – Last night, German leader Hitler announced the cancellation of appointments in the next ten days, because he needs to have important political discussions and has no time for other matters. This shows that Germany attaches great importance to the compromise reached by Britain and France in London on Sunday. As for what attitude Germany will take towards this, it seems that it has not yet reached a consensus. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs, led by von Neurath, still holds a friendly spirit of taking the London proposal as the basis for negotiations. The German leader also seems to welcome sincere discussions on this proposal, especially regarding the military aspect, in view of the recent widespread rumors abroad that Germany is secretly rearming. However, the opinions of the extreme National Socialists are that this proposal is mostly in conflict with the party's program, so there is a lot of criticism. The German ambassador to France, Köster, has now set off to return to his post, carrying a note to the French government asking for clarification on the various points in the proposal. (Reuters dispatch, 7th)

Optimism Lacking in Inducing Germany to Return to League of Nations 35

A report from Warsaw, by the semi-official Polish Daily, containing dispatches from London and Berlin, expresses considerable doubt about the future success of the international negotiations planned at the recent Anglo-French London conference. The London dispatch states that the British view has gone further than the Eastern European Pact, and aims not to encircle Germany but to induce it to rejoin the League of Nations. The dispatch further states that the London talks are merely the beginning of lengthy and difficult international negotiations, with France insisting on guarantees and Germany demanding equal rights. Britain hopes for successful disarmament, making mediation between the three difficult. The Berlin dispatch is even more pessimistic, stating that although the London conference has begun, the time when all relevant countries can gather at a round table is still far off. Furthermore, in the current situation, war may not be imminent, but the continuation of the arms race is to be expected. (National Telegram, 6th)

France Seeks Loans from Britain After Rejection of Currency Stabilization Proposal 36

London - According to usually reliable financial sources today, Premier Flandin hinted during his visit to London last week that France might seek loans from Britain. It is said that after the French Premier's suggestion to stabilize currency at an early date was rejected by financial circles and the Bank of England, he secretly informed the British authorities of this intention. It is recalled that the French government recently increased its short-term public debt from 10,000,000,000 francs to 15,000,000,000 francs. During Flandin's visit to London and negotiations on the Anglo-French agreement, he met with British government financial advisor, Chancellor of the Exchequer Chamberlain, and banker Blumenthal. It is now known that although Flandin did not explicitly request Britain to lift the ban on foreign loans, he indicated that France might seek loans from abroad to address its immediate needs. It is also learned that France will formally contact Britain and the Netherlands regarding this matter. (National Telegram, 6th)

Internal Strife in Hungarian Government Party 37

Opposing Political Views

Budapest, Hungary - Internal discord has broken out within the National Unity Party (the ruling party), and has now reached an acute stage. The party has split into two factions: one supporting Prime Minister Gömbös, and the other led by former Prime Minister Bethlen. The two factions hold divergent views on both domestic and foreign policy. For example, regarding the revision of Hungary's borders, both factions acknowledge its necessity, but General Gömbös advocates raising the issue in future international negotiations, while Bethlen believes that the time is not yet ripe. As for domestic policy, Bethlen strongly opposes Gömbös' proposed land reform and electoral reform bills. The key to the political situation now lies in the hands of Regent Horthy, as he has the power to dissolve parliament. In short, the infighting between the two factions within the ruling party is intensifying daily. One faction uses "Supporting Gömbös" as its slogan, while the Bethlen faction opposes him, claiming that Gömbös' actions have dangerous National Socialist tendencies. The outcome remains to be seen. (Havas Dispatch, 6th)

U.S. War Department's National Mobilization Plan 38

Submitted to Senate for Discussion

Washington - Democratic Senator Clark recently submitted the War Department's draft national mobilization plan to the Senate for discussion. This plan stipulates that all citizens over the age of eighteen are subject to conscription, and authorizes the government to control all industries deemed necessary during wartime. (Great Japan Havas Dispatch)

House Military Affairs Committee Passes Bill to Control Wartime Profits 39

Washington - The House of Representatives today unanimously approved the report on Representative McSwain's bill to control wartime profits. Washington believes this move is particularly noteworthy coming after the Senate Munitions Investigating Committee caused international conflicts. American Federation of Labor officials have supported the bill from the start, arguing that since the people have an obligation to serve in the military, industrial machinery and financial organizations should have the same obligation. Others see the Committee's actions as an attempt to clarify its position, which may not be entirely consistent with the War Department's plans released during the munitions investigation. Senator Nye, chairman of the Munitions Investigating Committee, claimed that munitions dealers were found to have made profits as high as 300%, and that during the European War, 181 Americans had incomes exceeding one million dollars each. Many foreign officials, identified by witnesses, protested the release of testimony and criticized the Committee's actions. However, the Investigating Committee's mission is not yet complete. With McSwain's proposal, further government action is expected based on the evidence collected by the Munitions Investigating Committee. The alleged conflict with the War Department's plans is limited to theoretical aspects, but officials who testified at previous committee investigation meetings stated that the War Department cooperated with munitions dealers to increase the development of the munitions industry without using government funds. Nye claimed that munitions dealers, driven by profit, directly or indirectly provoke international conflict. (National Telegram, 6th)

Preparing to Declare a State of Emergency

Seeking Legislative Remedy

Washington - Regarding the question of whether the abolition of the gold clause is valid, all parties are now awaiting the Supreme Court's decision. As a result, public opinion is quite hesitant. On the other hand, President Roosevelt continues to pursue his policy of economic centralization and rationalization. On the surface, if the Supreme Court's decision is unfavorable to the government and greatly weakens government authority, President Roosevelt will be constrained. Some bills that would face resistance before passage may not even be introduced. However, government officials have repeatedly stated that, if necessary, they are prepared to declare a state of emergency to remedy the consequences of the abolition of the gold clause. This attitude of the government has attracted much attention. The government may believe that only bold action is the best policy. Representative Rayburn, Chairman of the House Commerce Committee, has introduced a bill advocating government control of all public utilities, prohibiting monopolies, regulating gas and electricity businesses, and regulating domestic and foreign enterprises. (Havas Dispatch, 7th)

British Wirral By-election for House of Commons Seat 41

Labour Party Wins

Conservative Party Attaches Great Importance

London - A by-election for a seat in the House of Commons was held today in the Wirral constituency of Liverpool, England. There were four candidates: Labour's Cleary, the National Conservative Party's Platt, the Independent Conservative Churchill, and the Liberal Party's Marris. The Labour candidate won, receiving 15,611 votes. Newspapers commented on the event, calling it a major blow to the government. The division within the Conservative Party led to the Labour victory. The Independent Conservative Churchill is the son of the well-known politician Winston Churchill. He not only opposes the Indian Constitution Bill, but also criticizes the government's general policies. He received 10,575 votes. If Churchill had not formed his own party, the National Conservative Platt would have received more than 13,771 votes and could have defeated the Labour Party. This result will not only encourage the opposition to the Indian Constitution Bill, but also carries the possibility of Independent Conservatives interfering in other by-elections. Therefore, the Conservative Party attaches great importance to this matter. (Reuters Telegram, 7th)

Paris Uprising Anniversary, Communist Party Holds Large Demonstration 42

Military Police on Alert, No Serious Incidents Occur

1,200 Young People Arrested

Paris - The world's beautiful capital, Paris, experienced another tragedy today. A similar event occurred one year ago. More than 1,200 Communists were arrested, reportedly carrying pistols, bayonets, and oil-soaked rags. There were five injured. Police predicted that riots would continue. As of recently, there have been no reports of fatalities. Armed mounted police dispersed crowds attempting to storm the Presidential Palace and arrested 40 rioters. Police reports stated that rioters arrested outside the Presidential Palace were carrying guns, knives and clubs. The large demonstration took place near the Concorde Triangle area of Saint-Lazare. After receiving telegrams that Communist leaders were brewing a demonstration, officials mobilized reserves this morning. It is said that fortunately for this telegram, the incident was able to be quelled. Although today's events were very serious, they were far from comparable to last year's riots, in which many people were killed and injured. (National Telegram, 6th)

Paris - Yesterday marked the anniversary of last year's major disturbances in Paris. Police were on alert all day, and no serious incidents occurred. Only after a religious memorial service did several thousand young people sing the Marseillaise and clash with police, but they were eventually dispersed. Yesterday, 1,200 people were arrested, including many Communists carrying pistols. It is reported that they fired shots at the police near a church, but fortunately no one was injured. (Reuters Telegram, 7th) Paris - Yesterday marked the anniversary of last year's disturbances in Paris. The morning was quiet, but around midnight, a large number of Communist demonstrators, arriving by train, car and tram from various towns and villages near Paris, gathered in the Place de la Concorde. Around the Saint-Lazare station and Place de la Concorde, 565 people were arrested by the authorities. Most of them were carrying weapons, clubs and rags soaked in gasoline. At around 1 a.m., another 40 Communists were arrested near the Presidential Palace, mostly carrying pistols and knives. By 1:30 a.m., the total number of people arrested was 1,200. Last night, a large number of young patriots came to participate in the memorial service and cheered for Chiappe, the police chief who was dismissed last year, who also attended the meeting. Afterwards, they formed a line and marched to the Arc de Triomphe, placing flowers at the Tomb of the Unknown Soldier, and then made speeches using moderate language. The flowers placed at the Place de la Concorde yesterday morning were moved by the police chief to the cemetery where those who died last year were buried together. In short, yesterday's memorial passed peacefully in Paris and various provinces, with no incidents occurring. (Havas Telegram, 7th)

Tokyo - The French government implemented revised tariffs on cotton yarn and cotton products in Syria, its mandated territory, on November 21 of last year. British House of Commons Questions Guards on Shipping in China 45

London - During today's meeting of the House of Commons, Conservative MP MacDonagh asked the government to continue to consider placing guards on all ships, large and small, traveling in Chinese waters frequented by pirates, for the safety of travelers. He also asked whether protecting British ships in Chinese waters was the responsibility of the British Navy, and why shipping companies were not required to provide adequate guards on all their ships. The First Lord of the Admiralty, Sir Bolton Eyres Monsell, replied that the British naval authorities in China are making every effort to ensure that British shipping companies provide adequate guards on all ships traveling along the Chinese coast. There is a difference between British ships sailing on the high seas and those sailing on inland waters. Those sailing on the Yangtze River are provided with guards by the British authorities, while those sailing on the high seas, such as the Tongzhou ships, are guarded by the shipping companies themselves. However, in special circumstances, naval guards are also provided by us. MacDonagh also asked whether the British Navy often goes to the rescue when British ships are attacked by pirates. The First Lord replied in the affirmative. The First Lord continued to say that after receiving detailed reports of the piracy on the Tongzhou, the circumstances of the Tongzhou's misfortune will be thoroughly investigated in London. Conservative MP Lord Apsley also asked Foreign Secretary Simon whether he should suggest to the Chinese government to negotiate a joint effort to suppress piracy in Chinese waters. Simon replied that the British Navy in China is already taking joint action with the Chinese army and navy, and this cooperation has been effective. Given the close relationship between the Chinese and British navies and their cooperation, I believe that the government does not need to take further action. The Foreign Secretary also answered another question from Conservative MP Knox, saying that according to a telegram from Nanjing on December 27 of last year, the danger of bandit-communist activity in the Yangtze River area between Hankou and Nanjing has been eliminated, so the safety of ships and passengers is no longer a concern. However, the British Consul and naval authorities will continue to pay attention to the overall situation. (Reuters Telegram, 6th)

Yang Hucheng Returns to Xi'an 46

Xi'an - Yang Hucheng went to southern Shaanxi last year to inspect defenses. In mid-January, he went to Zhen'an and Shangxian to oversee the suppression of the Xu Haidong bandits and to rectify the discipline of the bandit suppression troops. After overseeing his troops, he defeated the Xu bandits. Only over a thousand bandits remain, and they have now fled to the Baihe and Yunxi areas on the border between Hubei and Shaanxi. Yang believed that the bandit suppression had come to an end, and ordered three brigade commanders, Liu Yanbiao, Zhang Hongyuan, and Tang Sitong, to be responsible for continuing the suppression. As he had been away from the province for a long time and military affairs urgently needed to be handled, he departed from the Shangxian headquarters at 3:00 PM on the 6th and returned to Xi'an. People from all walks of life came to the suburbs to welcome him. According to Yang, the defenses in southern Shaanxi have been properly arranged during his two-month absence from the province. Most of the Xu bandits have been defeated by us, and the Shaanxi army and Xiao Zhichu's troops are continuing to clear them out, which will happen soon. The bandit suppression in southern Shaanxi has been successful. Sun Weiru is now in charge, commanding everything. The Shaanxi army has entered Sichuan to assist in the suppression, and the counties of Wanyuan and Chengkou will soon be recovered. There are no longer any traces of bandits in northeastern Sichuan. The Shaanxi army has a specific plan for entering Sichuan. The bandits near Guangyuan, Raoning and Qiang were defeated by us. The Shaanxi army has established contact with Hu Zongnan, Xiao Zhichu and other troops, and is determined to jointly suppress the Red bandits in northern Sichuan. (Central Telegram, 7th)

Foreigners Prohibited from Excavating Antiquities Within China 58

The Nanjing Antiquities Preservation Committee has telegraphed to various provincial governments stating: Foreigners coming to China for travel often use various pretexts to privately excavate antiquities, resulting in significant losses to our nation's history and culture. Hereafter, foreign nationals, regardless of the capacity, are prohibited from excavating antiquities within Chinese territory. Even in cases where foreign academic organizations or individuals provide financial assistance to Chinese academic institutions for the excavation of antiquities, the academic institution must report to this committee, and only upon approval may they accept such assistance. Please instruct your provincial government to carefully observe the enforcement regulations of the Antiquities Preservation Law and pay close attention to foreign nationals entering the country for travel. (7th - Special Dispatch)

American Students Test War and Peace Psychology 95

The Tokyo Asahi Shimbun reported that a special correspondent in New York sent a cable stating that the American student peace theory test vote, jointly initiated by the weekly magazine Literary Review and the University News Editors Association, was held to understand the psychology of American students regarding the current world situation. Among the 32,500 votes received, the majority supported peace. The content is as follows: (1) Does the United States face the possibility of being drawn into the vortex of war in the future? As a result, 20,154 votes believed there was a possibility of being drawn in, while 9,731 votes opposed. (2) If the United States is invaded by other countries, would you be willing to take up arms and fight? 24,291 votes supported resistance, while 5,408 votes opposed resistance. (3) What are your thoughts on the United States invading other countries? 24,508 votes advocated not invading other countries, while 4,982 votes supported it. (4) Is the doctrine of the United States Navy and Air Force reaching the world's leading position a sound policy for preventing participation in war? 9,931 votes supported it, while 20,031 votes opposed it. (5) Can the United States join the League of Nations? 15,731 votes supported it, while 14,072 votes opposed it. From the above, it can be seen that in this test of American students' psychology towards war and peace, the opposition to the doctrine of the United States Navy and Air Force being the world's leading power was at a ratio of two to one, which clearly shows the peace-loving nature of American youth.

Jiangxi Province Military Rice Transferred to Regulate Civilian Food Supply 97

Purchased by the Provincial Government with Prepared Funds

Nanchang correspondence: During the tense period of the suppression of the Red Army in Jiangxi Province, the armies that joined the battle sequence, in the east, west, north, and south, numbered no fewer than [blank] tens of thousands of people. Therefore, the Logistics Office of the Campaign Headquarters made full preparations in advance for military food, purchasing it in various places where rice prices were lower. Grain reserves were extremely abundant in the military centers. Now that the suppression of the Red Army has concluded, the battle sequence has been dissolved, and a portion of the armies have entered Hunan, Guizhou, and Sichuan to continue the suppression. The cities of Ji'an and Nancheng have dispatched 120,000 dan of military rice. The local authorities in the province have decided to purchase this military rice with prepared funds and transport it to the most food-scarce drought and bandit-stricken areas to regulate the civilian food supply. After the bandit disaster in the 7th year of the Republic, coupled with the unprecedented drought last year, the harvest of early and late rice crops was less than half of normal, creating a famine-like scene not seen in fifty years. A survey of civilian food in various places by the Civil Affairs Department shows that the majority of people are short of food for more than four months, and in counties such as Ruichang, Hukou, and Xingzi in northern Jiangxi, even grass roots and tree bark have been exhausted. A large-scale and comprehensive relief effort is necessary to avert a catastrophe. Therefore, the Civil Affairs Department and the Finance Department have prepared funds to purchase and transport this 120,000 dan of foreign rice to famine areas as the first step. The second step will be to manage grain price regulation at the time when the old harvest has been consumed and new crops are still growing, using the accumulated grain from various places that was organized last year. It is reported that the Jiangxi Office of the Economic Commission and the Rural Cooperative Association will use a portion of the cooperative funds for grain transportation and marketing cooperation. In addition, the first batch of 20,000 bags of relief rice from the Shanghai Red Swastika Society's drought relief effort has been transported to Jiujiang and is being inspected and released by Li Dixian and others.

Xiamen to Establish Municipal Government 98

Political Council Orders Provincial Government to Investigate and Report

Civil Affairs Department Has Already Prepared the Municipal Government Organization

Xiamen correspondence: Xiamen is one of the earliest five treaty ports. Its commercial and economic status in South China ranks third, only after Guangzhou and Shantou. The total value of customs trade reaches more than 30 million yuan per year, with tax revenue of more than 4 million yuan. Therefore, the proposal to establish a municipal government has been around for a long time. However, the reason why it has not been realized is that the ordinary city establishment in the National Government's city organization law requires a population of more than 200,000, and the total amount of business tax, license fees, and land tax collected annually accounts for more than one-half of the total income of the area. However, the population of Xiamen City is more than 170,000, which is less than 200,000, and the revenue from business licenses, land, and other taxes is not large. Therefore, the establishment of a municipal government cannot be financially self-sufficient. Therefore, during the period when Yang Shuzhuang governed Fujian, the matter was repeatedly discussed but not completed. When the 19th Route Army entered Fujian, it decided to establish a city and had already established the (Siming Municipal Government Preparatory Office). It was planned to merge Siming County and rename the entire island of Xiamen as Siming Municipal Government. Subsequently, the Executive Yuan submitted the matter to the Navy, the Ministry of Interior, and the Ministry of Foreign Affairs for review. After deliberation by the three ministries, for diplomatic and national defense reasons, Heshan was still under the Siming County Government as an inland area. Only the urban area under the jurisdiction of the current Xiamen Public Security Bureau was established as a municipal government. The matter was not realized and the Fujian Incident occurred, so it was not carried out. After the Central Army recovered Xiamen, the provincial government felt that there was a definite need for unified administration in terms of internal affairs and foreign affairs, and the matter was indeed beyond the scope of what a county government could encompass. Therefore, the (Xiamen Special Public Security Bureau) was established in the Xiamen urban area, and Wang Gupan was appointed as the director, which was a transformed municipal government. The Siming County Government still existed, and Wang concurrently served as the county magistrate, so as to unify local administrative power. Later, the provincial government submitted the case of establishing the (Xiamen Special Public Security Bureau) to the Executive Yuan. After discussion at the Executive Council, it was decided that the whole country only had Weihaiwei, which had recovered a concession and established a special public security bureau. Since Xiamen did not have any special circumstances, it was impossible to establish a special public security bureau. As a result, the application was rejected. Last winter, Wang Gupan personally went to Nanjing to explain the situation to the central government and requested to resign. The central government retained him and ordered him to return to his post. At the same time, the provincial government submitted the proposal for the establishment of a municipal government to the Executive Yuan again. The Executive Yuan approved the order for the provincial government to investigate the situation in Xiamen and submit a report for review. The provincial government held two meetings at the end of the year and discussed this matter for a long time, ordering the Civil Affairs Department to handle it. The Civil Affairs Department has already prepared the organization, established a municipal government, and established one bureau and three sections, namely: (1) the Public Security Bureau; (2) the First Section, managing matters related to opium suppression, sanitation, charity, land, autonomy, and ethics and education; (3) the Second Section, managing matters related to finance, public property, public operations, food, and other matters; and (4) the Third Section, managing matters related to public utilities, construction, transportation, industry, and education. After the proposal is submitted to the provincial government meeting for approval, it can be reported to the Executive Yuan. The date of Xiamen's establishment as a city should not be far away. (6th)

Guangxi Province Reorganizes Civilian Fire Protection 99

Each County and City Organizes a Civilian Fire Protection Association

Civilians Have the Responsibility of Voluntary Firefighting

Guangzhou correspondence: Guangxi Province's civilian defense training has achieved considerable results. Recently, since civilian fire protection and air defense construction have a great relationship, the Guangxi Construction Committee has specially proposed the establishment of the Guangxi Civilian Fire Protection Committee. It has prepared general rules and survey forms for government-run and private fire protection, and submitted them to the Guangxi Provincial Government for approval. Yesterday, orders have been issued to various counties and cities for separate compliance. The attached organizational general rules are as follows:

Article 1: Each city and county, for the purpose of eliminating fires, should organize a civilian fire protection committee (hereinafter referred to as the Fire Protection Committee) to handle civilian fire protection matters under the direction of the local competent authorities (such as the Public Security Bureau, County Government, District, Township, and Town Office, etc.). Article 2: Each Fire Protection Committee should be named after the local place. Article 3: The Fire Protection Association shall have five to nine members, with one to three members appointed by the local competent authority, and the remainder elected by the representatives of all sectors. The term of office for elected members is one year, and they may be re-elected. Article 4: The Fire Protection Association shall have one to three standing committee members, one of whom shall be elected by the appointed members, and if there are three, one shall be elected by the appointed members and two by the elected members. Article 5: The Fire Protection Committee shall appoint several fire squad leaders and drivers, and their number shall be determined according to local conditions and the complexity of affairs. Article 6: Each fire squad shall have several members, who shall be selected by the committee from the able-bodied men over the age of eighteen and under the age of fifty residing in the area on a rotational basis, and appointed by the competent authority for a term of one year. They shall have the responsibility of voluntary firefighting. In the event of a fire alarm, they must quickly go to their respective squad to assemble and, led by the squad leader, rush to the disaster site to put out the fire. Article 7: The squad leader and driver may be given an appropriate allowance by the committee's resolution. Article 8: The methods for raising funds for civilian fire protection shall be formulated by the Fire Protection Association and submitted to the local competent authority for review and approval, and then submitted to the government at each level for approval before they can be implemented. Article 9: The existing civilian fire protection organizations in each city and county shall be reorganized in accordance with these general rules. Article 10: The detailed rules for the operation of the Fire Protection Association should be formulated by the committee and reported to the local competent authority for review and approval, and then submitted to the provincial government at each level for review and filing. Article 11: These general rules shall be implemented from the date of promulgation. (February 2)

General Situation of Changting Papermaking 100

Annual production of over 20,000 piculs, ranking first among local products

Establishment of a Publicly Operated Paper Company for Continued Operation

Xiamen Communication: Western Fujian is a paper-producing region. Before the lifting of the maritime ban, its products such as (Lianshi) paper were sold throughout the country, especially Changting. Most of the paper produced in Changting was exported to Chaoshan via the Han River. Although Western paper has become popular in recent years, there is still a considerable demand for domestic paper such as Lianshi and Maobian. Therefore, the production volume is still abundant, ranking first among Changting's local products. After Changting fell to the bandits, in November of the 22nd year [of the Republic], the Zhonghua Commercial Company of the pseudo-Central Government in Ruijin specially organized a paper company, appointing a person from Xingguo as manager, with a capital of 200,000 yuan. They once smuggled a part of their products through the Tinghang blockade line of the pseudo-Commercial Company and transported them to Chaoshan for sale, making considerable profits. After the National Army recovered Changting, this bandit property was investigated and confiscated, and the third temporary meeting of the Post-War Relief Committee resolved to establish a (Publicly Operated Paper Company). Currently, the company's address is located at the Fan Family Ancestral Hall on Zhongzheng Road in Changting, and it officially opened for business on December 21. According to the person in charge of the company, the detailed accounts of the former pseudo-paper company have all been lost, and the amounts of paper for each trough cannot be verified. However, there are still vouchers for each trough, which are temporarily used as a basis. The paper production area also covers the territory of Jiangxi Province, including Tailai, Ridong, Yangdi, and Taoyang in Jiangxi, and Guanqianjia, Liangfang, Sibu, Dongpo Zhangdi, Changning, Zhenhua, and Qigushuxia in Fujian, totaling twelve areas with two hundred and thirty-eight troughs. Among the areas, Changning has the most paper troughs, with twenty-four troughs, producing more than 9,000 piculs annually. In total, the capital of each trough was about 100,000 yuan during the former pseudo-paper company, and the paper production was more than 20,000 piculs. After the establishment and registration of the publicly operated paper company, areas such as Zhangdi have come to register, totaling more than 9,000 piculs. The Changning area has also been surveyed. Other areas are temporarily suspended due to unsettled local conditions. About 300 piculs of paper have been paid, and they are currently stored and not yet sold. (February 6)

Telephone Damage After Heavy Snow in Songjiang 102

Yesterday (6th) morning at 10:00 AM, spring snow suddenly fell in this city, pressing on the high-voltage wires of electric lights and touching the telephone lines. The current spread, and for a while, the telephones in the households suddenly heard a long ringing that lasted for dozens of minutes. At the telephone company's switchboard, dozens of number plates suddenly emitted smoke, filling the machine room. The company authorities, realizing there was a problem, immediately telegraphed the electric light company to temporarily close the power supply switches on all lines to check for damage and carry out repairs. However, the electric light company did not grant the request, and all the number plates of the telephone switchboard were smoking, indicating a serious situation. The telephone company, fearing the risk of electric shock to users, cut the telephone main line to prevent the current. The company then informed the users, temporarily suspending calls, and dispatched workers to repair the damage in all directions. It is feared that it will not be completed in three or four days.

County Government Convened Merchants and Baojia to Investigate Population 103

The county ordered the implementation of Baojia [system], and from November 25th of last year, each district uniformly started compiling household registers, which has been completed on schedule. Baojia heads have been successively elected, and the election of township and town heads is currently underway. The second phase of work in this county has been completed, and the third phase of population investigation and the handling of joint security procedures should continue. Therefore, the county government has scheduled to convene the district chiefs, assistant officers, and compilation and investigation committee members at 2:00 PM on the 12th of this month to discuss the progress of the third phase of Baoli [neighborhood] work.

Namhui Peasant Killed While Capturing Thieves Empty-Handed 104

Zhao Desan's family, farmers of Yanlou Township, District 1, about three miles outside the South Gate of this city, were suddenly visited by more than a dozen thieves speaking the local dialect around 12:00 PM the night before last. Because there were many people in the house, they all came out to resist the thieves, so the thieves did not have time to plunder, only stealing a gold ring and dozens of beads before escaping. Zhao's nephew, Zhang Fu, was courageous and went out to pursue the fleeing thieves. After walking about half a li, he caught a thief and fought him empty-handed, but was shot in the left forehead by the thief and immediately fell to the ground and died. Upon receiving the report, County Magistrate Yuan immediately ordered the police to strictly arrest the murderers and bring them to justice. He also personally wrote the four characters "Sacrifice Life for Righteousness," added a postscript, and presented it as a commendation.

Two Pawnshops in Wuxi Close Down in Succession 105

Since the failure of the silk factory industry in this county, all industries have been affected, and business has plummeted, causing great depression in society. During this period of major closure, the number of industries that have closed down or been consolidated is unknown. It is learned that the Gongshun Pawnshop in Yingqiao Lane and the Chunhua Pawnshop in Huangni Village outside the South Gate, both owned by Sheng Yifan of Changzhou, have been in operation for several decades. In recent years, due to sluggish business and financial difficulties, they announced their closure from the previous day, only redeeming items and not accepting new ones, until the end of this year. Yesterday, a special report was submitted to the county government for record.

Investigation of Rice and Paddy Stored in Warehouses 106

Last year, the early rice disaster caused a poor harvest of rice and grain. However, the stocks in various warehouses in this county have not decreased. The reason is that the rural economy is exhausted. Once the rice and paddy are harvested, they are immediately transported to the market for sale, exchanged for cash, or used by merchants to deposit in warehouses for loans. The reporter has investigated the rice and grain stored in 26 warehouses in this county (excluding four warehouses in the Southern District that were not included in the investigation) as follows, to inform those who care about people's food: 524,950 piculs of Geng rice, 483,270 piculs of Xian rice, 163,240 piculs of Yuan rice, 100,258 shi of manufactured Geng rice, 49,714 shi of manufactured Xian rice, 11,500 shi of manufactured Yuan rice, 34,560 shi of white Xian rice, 270 shi of white Geng rice, 2,140 shi of white Yuan rice, 394,600 shi of soybeans, 64,540 shi of mung beans, 133,160 bags of wheat, 69,110 piculs of barley, 16,380 shi of Yuan wheat, 900 piculs of wild rice, 1,460 shi of Saigon rice, 19,600 shi of sorghum, 14,800 shi of sesame, 3,730 shi of corn, 230 shi of broad beans, 1,200 shi of red beans.

Negotiations Regarding the Collision of the Qingning Steamer and a Sampan 107

Wang Yuanji Foundry in Yanqiao Town in this county and Tong Yuanji Foundry in Xicangqiao, Changzhou, are affiliated, owned by the same owner, and have distribution points in Wuxi, Changzhou, Nantong and other counties. Wang Yuanji North Warehouse, the Nantong distribution point, long-term hired Tang Jikang's sampan to transport iron pots and other goods between Changzhou and Nantong for sale, transporting more than ten times a year. When returning from Nantong to Wuxi and Changzhou, the sampan also transported cotton and other sundries to maintain expenses. Tang Jikang and his son had been transporting iron pots for the two foundries for decades and were very careful, greatly trusted by the foundry owner. On the first of this month, the sampan loaded with iron pots from Wuxi and Changzhou set off from Wuxi to Nantong. The next morning, while sailing on the river near Jiangyin, it suddenly encountered the Qingning steamer of Shanghai Zhongning Company (some say Huaxing) heading to Pukou, which came from behind. The sampan was unable to avoid it in time, and the stern of the sampan was hit and broken into two sections. All five people on board were unable to escape. The Qingning steamer, realizing it had caused an accident, sped away without rescuing the people. Later, another ship passed by and complained greatly, issuing an alarm for help. The Qingning steamer then began to rescue the people. At that time, three people were rescued, but Tang Jikang and another person were drowned. The people on the Qingning steamer forced the three rescued people to sign a document, the purpose of which is unknown. After the incident, the survivors went to Jiangyin and then to Wuxi to report to Sun Boying and Yu Daiqing, the managers of Wuxi and Changzhou, who entrusted lawyer Yun Kuyao, their perennial legal counsel, to send a letter to the Shanghai Collision Ship Committee and lodge a serious protest with the Zhongning Company. The total loss is estimated at five or six thousand yuan, and two people drowned, which is truly tragic.

Jiangyin County Order Dismisses Three Section Chiefs 108

Cui Hualiang, Chief of the Third Section of the County Government, and technician Yang Jiandong, were appointed after the Construction Bureau was merged into the Third Section. Now they have been accused by someone in the province. After investigation, the accusations were found to be true, and the Provincial Government ordered their dismissal. Chen Bingzhang (a native of this county) has been appointed as the Chief of the Third Section and has officially assumed office.

Yangzhou Cracked a Robbery and Kidnapping Case 109

Zhang Qing'an, the leader of the First Detective Group of the Jiangdu Public Security Bureau, due to the county magistrate's personal order to solve the city and rural robbery cases, led detectives to Zhenjiang and joined Captain Cai of the Detective Team of the Provincial Public Security Bureau. At Sishi Bailing Ferry, they disguised themselves and captured notorious bandits Di Liu (alias Di Xuezheng), Yang Xueming, Xu Huaiguo, and Tao Haicheng. They seized a self-defense gun in the case of the murder of Ma Jingren, a villager of Yangwan Township, and a six-shot revolver and two pawn tickets at Ma Wenming's house in Xianzhen. They were handed over to the Public Security Bureau. During the interrogation, they confessed to the murder of Ma Jingren and also confessed to the robbery of Zhou Dekuan's house in Maqiao and Guo Jilin's house in Yinjiagou. Yesterday (5th), they were handed over to the county by the bureau for disposition.

General Situation of Profits and Losses in Various Industries in Xiaoshan 110

After the major closure of businesses in Xiaoshan County, the most profitable industries were the sauce industry and the tofu industry, followed by the money industry, and then the southern goods industry and the rice industry. The oil and candle industry, grocery industry, foreign and Guang goods, calico industry, pastry industry, and cured meat industry were average. The copper and tin industry and the woodenware industry were unprofitable. Due to years of famine, people simplified everything related to weddings, so those who were usually well-off reduced their expenses by more than half last winter, resulting in an abnormal decline in business. The remaining restaurants and dim sum shops were also unprofitable due to account problems.

The Trial of the Gruesome Murder Case in Qianyao, Jiashan, Will Open Soon 111

After the prosecutor sent by the court to Qianyao Town inspected the gruesome murder case, it was found that the deceased Zhang Chen had as many as forty-two knife wounds on her body. After investigation, Huang Dajie, a friend of Chen's before her death, is highly suspected. Huang Dajie's husband and A Wu from Taizhou are also suspects. It can be seen that there are many accomplices in this case, involving a wide range of people. All the suspects have been arrested and brought to the court, and the trial will open soon.

Suspects in the Shi Liangcai Case in Hangzhou Will Be Sent to the Province 112

Xu Yan, the director of the Public Security Bureau of Haining County, the county in charge of the assassination case of Mr. Shi Liangcai, the general manager of this newspaper, was assassinated on the Shanghai-Hangzhou highway, went to Shanghai several times to investigate and arrest the suspects. Therefore, personnel were dispatched to Nanhui to bring Song Miaosheng, who is expected to arrive tomorrow or the day after, and they will be sent to the province together for interrogation.

Since the beginning of winter, the weather in Hangzhou has been mild, like spring, and the thermometer has often been above 40 degrees. Businesses Reopen After Spring Festival Holiday 115

Bankrupt shops double those of last year

After handling the general closing of accounts on February 3, the industrial and commercial sectors of this city, following the old customs, announced a holiday from February 4. Yesterday, some shops began to open for business, and all businesses will reopen today. However, some shops will delay reopening for reorganization or announce liquidation due to the impact of the recession. The details are recorded as follows:

Shops Open for Business 116

From February 4th to 6th, all businesses in this city announced a holiday, and all factories also stopped work. However, general entertainment venues remained open as usual and enjoyed a hundredfold profit. Department stores, pharmacies, bookstores, southern goods stores, as well as tobacco shops, grocery stores, and restaurants, began to reopen yesterday morning.

Banks Reopen 117

All banks in this city have a four-day holiday from February 4th and will reopen on the 8th. The exchanges will also open on the same day to resume trading. Therefore, all businesses in the city will reopen from the 8th.

Closed Businesses 118

Central Bank to Build a Qujiang Wharf Warehouse 126

Collecting 2,500 mu of land in accordance with the law

Approved by the Ministry of Interior and announced for public knowledge

The Ministry of Interior issued an announcement regarding the Central Bank's collection of land in Shanghai for the construction of a port, stating that the Central Bank's official letter No. 1635 states that, in order to revitalize industry and promote the development of international trade, the bank plans to build a Qujiang wharf warehouse and operate industries related to the wharf. However, the bank's existing land at the mouth of the Qujiang is not enough for construction, and it is proposed to collect about 2,500 mu of land adjacent to the Central Bank's wharf area at the mouth of the Qujiang in Shanghai, bordered by the Central Bank's wharf property to the east, Jungong Road to the west, the Qujiang River to the south, and the Xiajiabang River to the north, in accordance with the law, for filling and construction to provide for the future establishment of factories and warehouses. The plan map is attached, and we request your ministry to consult with the Shanghai Municipal Government for review and reply. Upon review, this complies with the provisions of Article 2, Paragraphs 3 and 8 of the Land Expropriation Law and should be approved. In addition to consulting with the Shanghai Municipal Government for review and replying to the Central Bank, please also follow the provisions of Article 9 of the same law and list the matters to be announced below so that everyone knows. The details are: 1. The person running the business: Central Bank. 2. The nature of the business: construction of a port and expansion of state-owned industry and commerce. 3. The location of the business: Qujiang Mouth, Shanghai, adjacent to the Central Bank's wharf property to the east, Jungong Road to the west, the Qujiang River to the south, and the Xiajiabang River to the north, with an estimated area of 2,500 mu.

Shanghai Telephone Bureau of the Ministry of Transportation and Shanghai Telephone Company Sign Long-Distance Telephone Connection Contract 127

Signed yesterday morning at 10:00 AM at the Shanghai Telephone Bureau

Effective for a period of five years upon signing

Recently, the Ministry of Transportation, considering that the previous long-distance connection contract signed between the Shanghai Telephone Bureau and the Shanghai Telephone Company had expired, and to facilitate long-distance telephone calls for citizens in the concession areas, as well as to develop domestic and international long-distance telephone business, deemed it urgent to renew the contract for compliance. It is heard that the Ministry of Transportation, the Telephone Bureau, and the Company have consulted repeatedly and finalized the contract, which was approved by the Ministry of Transportation. On the morning of the 7th, at 10:00 AM, the manager of the Shanghai Telephone Company, a Westerner named Baud, along with Vice President Tan Xuewei, went to the Shanghai Telephone Bureau to formally sign the contract with the Bureau Director Xu Xueyu and German engineer Yu Bingjian. It is also heard that both parties will increase the number of long-distance relay lines within days, and will also open telephone access to various locations in the concession areas that are currently unable to connect, to facilitate communication. The original text of the contract is excerpted below:

Long-Distance Telephone Connection Contract 128

This contract is made on the 7th day of February in the 24th year of the Republic of China, corresponding to the 7th day of February in the year 1935 of the Western calendar, between the Shanghai Telephone Bureau of the Ministry of Transportation of the Republic of China (hereinafter referred to as "the Bureau," and as Party A) and the Shanghai Telephone Company, registered in the State of Delaware, USA, located at 232 Jiangxi Road, Shanghai, China (hereinafter referred to as "the Company," and as Party B). It is understood that the Bureau currently operates the local telephone service in Shanghai and can connect with the Ministry of Transportation's current and future domestic and international wired and wireless long-distance telephone services (hereinafter collectively referred to as "the Bureau's Lines"). The Company currently operates the local telephone service within the Shanghai International Settlement and the French Concession. Both parties believe that connecting with each other to exchange long-distance telephone calls, in accordance with the conditions outlined in this contract, will undoubtedly promote the interests of both parties and the public. Both parties, therefore, agree to enter into the following contract: 1. The Company's Lines shall connect with the Bureau's Lines at the boundary of Zhabei. The Company is responsible for the construction, maintenance, and operation of the lines from the long-distance station in the concession area to the boundary of Zhabei. The Bureau is responsible for the construction, maintenance, and operation of the lines from the long-distance station in Zhabei to the boundary of Zhabei. 2. Each party shall establish and maintain appropriate operational procedures to ensure that users of both parties can have rapid and direct communication with each other. 3. Within the scope of telephone services stipulated in this contract, the methods, rules, and accounting procedures for communication shall be determined by mutual agreement between the two parties. 4. Both parties shall each build, maintain, and operate their own telephone organizations to ensure that public telephone services are maintained in good condition, and each party shall independently or through the other party supply long-distance and exchange equipment. However, neither party shall be liable to the other for any damages arising from line obstructions or interruptions, regardless of the cause or duration of such obstructions or interruptions. Should such obstructions or interruptions occur, the Bureau and the Company shall make every effort to repair them within the shortest possible time. 5. The telephone charges for all calls shall be collected in accordance with the tariffs prescribed by the Ministry of Transportation as notified by the Bureau from time to time. Except for the appropriate special delivery fees that may be charged when it is necessary to dispatch a special messenger to notify the recipient, neither party may collect any other fees. The Bureau shall be responsible for notifying the Company of the tariffs prescribed by the Ministry of Transportation at least thirty days before the implementation of such tariffs. Except for necessary official calls between the Bureau and the Company, there shall be no free calls or discounts on telephone charges. All other calls shall still be calculated according to the prescribed tariffs. If the tariffs are not calculated in Chinese national currency, the Bureau shall notify the Company of the exchange rate for the month on the first day of each month so that the Company can collect fees from its users in Chinese national currency. 6. All incoming and outgoing telephone charges shall belong to the Bureau. The remuneration paid to the Company is as follows: A. For each long-distance telephone call (including notification fee) originated by the Company to the Bureau, the Company shall receive 10% of the total call charge or notification fee as a handling fee for originating the call, but the minimum handling fee shall not be less than five Chinese national currency cents, and the maximum shall not exceed one Chinese national currency dollar and fifty cents. B. For each long-distance telephone call (including notification fee) originated by the Bureau to the Company, the Company shall receive 5% of the total call charge or notification fee as a handling fee for terminating the call, but the minimum handling fee shall not be less than five Chinese national currency cents, and the maximum shall not exceed one Chinese national currency dollar and fifty cents. 7. For all telephone charges originating from one party to the other, both parties shall collect the charges from their own users and shall be fully responsible for the accounts and liabilities owed to the other party. Each party shall keep separate records of all items handled, and the other party may inspect these records and documents at any reasonable time. Each party shall prepare a monthly report on the telephone charges for the month and submit it to the other party by the end of the following month at the latest. This monthly report shall contain all items agreed upon by both parties from time to time. 8. If the party receiving a monthly report does not raise any written objections within one month after the monthly report is prepared and sent by one party to the other, it shall be deemed to have been acknowledged. The net difference between the telephone charges issued by both parties shall be paid by the paying party no later than the end of the second month following the month of the telephone call. 9. If the Company or the Bureau fails to pay any amount due in accordance with this contract, and fails to pay within thirty days after the other party submits a written notice to its head office, the other party may terminate this contract immediately by written notice to the head office of that party. 10. The failure of either party to comply with or implement, or the failure of the other party to insist on compliance with any provision of this contract, or the waiver by either party of any provision of this contract under any circumstances, shall not be deemed to be a joint abandonment of such provision. Such provision shall always retain its full force and effect. 11. If the parties cannot agree on the implementation of any provision of this contract, the matter shall be submitted to an arbitration committee. One party shall notify the other party in writing of the name of the arbitrator it has selected and inquire about the arbitrator selected by the other party. Within ten days of receiving the written notice, the other party shall inform the first party of the name of its arbitrator, and the arbitrators appointed by both parties shall jointly select a third arbitrator. If the two arbitrators are unable to agree on the selection of a third arbitrator after twenty days, both parties shall request the non-American head of the Shanghai Consular Body to appoint one. Both parties shall abide by the decision of the arbitrators. The arbitration costs shall be handled in accordance with the method determined by the arbitrators. 12. Without the written permission of the other party, neither party may transfer or assign this contract or any rights contained therein. Any assignment without the permission of the other party shall be deemed invalid. 13. This contract, except as provided in Article 9, shall be effective for a period of five years from the date of signing. After five years, it may not be terminated unless either party gives six months' prior written notice. 14. This contract is written in Chinese and is accompanied by an English translation agreed to by both parties. Both parties shall perform this contract after signing. This contract is signed and implemented by both parties on the 7th day of February in the 24th year of the Republic of China, corresponding to the 7th day of February in the year 1935 of the Western calendar, in the presence of witnesses. Shanghai Telephone Bureau of the Ministry of Transportation: Xu Xueyu (seal), Witness: Yu Bingjian, Shanghai Telephone Company: (concurrently) General Manager Baud, Witness: Tan Xuewei.
