The Chinese Science Society Held the Shanghai Alumni Congress Yesterday 225

Cai Yuanpei, Wang Yunwu, and Others Gave Speeches

Ding Xielin Described the Improved Chinese Flute

There Were Also High-Class Music and Factory Gifts

The Chinese Science Society held the Shanghai Alumni Congress and the 24th Alumni Friendship Meeting at the International Hotel at 6 PM yesterday (6th). More than two hundred alumni and their families attended, and the hall on the second floor was completely full.

Celebrity Speeches The dinner started at 7 PM. After coffee was served, Chairman Cao Liangxia delivered the opening remarks. According to the program of the conference, there were three speakers and seven musical performances interspersed. Cai Jiemin spoke about the two characters 乙亥, describing the important events of the year 乙亥 in history, and from the meaning of the characters 乙亥, he talked about arithmetic machines, animals, and plants, quoting scriptures and classics, broadly and mixed with humor, making the audience laugh. Next, Wang Yunwu gave a speech entitled "Mr. Science," briefly saying that this person has twelve sons, including arithmetic, astronomy, geography, and chemistry, and also a youngest son called "Learning Management." The Commercial Press was destroyed by the national crisis of January 28th. Fortunately, this young gentleman was invited to help, and it was able to revive. He hoped that in the future, instead of holding deity parades and seeking bodhisattvas, it would be better to pick up Mr. Science and let the people recognize him, as he is indeed our good advisor.

Improved National Flute Next, physicist Ding Xunfu spoke about the improved Chinese flute, briefly saying that the improvement of the Chinese flute has three prerequisites: 1. The intervals must be accurate. 2. The range must be increased. 3. The price of the flute must be low. Foreign flutes use keys to open and close, using ten fingers, and the range is naturally large, but a good flute costs 500 yuan each, which is not a way to popularize folk music. Based on his research results, he has completed several types of flutes, including those in C, B, and A keys, those made of copper, those made of bamboo, those with an inner diameter of two centimeters, and those with an inner diameter of 1.8 centimeters. The range is so large that 32 to 36 notes can be blown out from the lowest to the highest note, that is, 3 octaves, and each octave has 12 notes including semitones. He also performed with three bamboo flutes on the spot.

Performance Entertainment The musical performances that evening were all performed by Shanghai's first-class musicians. Miss Bao Kezhen opened the performance with a piano solo, followed by a chorus by Ms. Kawakli, and Ms. Bai Yemu Gan. Su Xulin, a professor at the National Academy of Music, sang a solo, Miss Gao Lan played a piano solo, Ms. Huali Si sang a solo, violin expert Professor Hua played three pieces, and finally Professor Chen Nengfang from the National Academy of Music sang to close the curtain.

Manufacturer Gifts The manufacturers who gave gifts to the conference included Yuanyuan Weaving Company, Chinese Science Company, Commercial Press, China and the West Pharmacy, Tianchu MSG Factory, Chinese Chemical Industry Society, Family Industry Society, Nanyang Brothers Tobacco Company, Shanghai Sheep Milk Company, Apple Electric Company, and more than ten other companies, with a total of more than 2,000 gifts. Among them, such as Yuanyuan meal towels, Science Company hardcover notebooks, China and the West One Drop Fragrance, Chemical Industry Society Era Cream, Family Industry Society Butterfly Cream, and old-brand MSG were all very popular. The whole audience also drank sheep's milk together and smoked Platinum Dragon cigarettes, which was particularly characteristic.

The Children's Welfare Association Asks the National Government to Promulgate a National Children's Year as Soon as Possible 226

And Set April 4th as the Opening Date

Order All Provinces to Hold Large-Scale Celebrations

The Shanghai Children's Welfare Association believes that this year is the National Children's Year, but the National Government has not yet issued a clear order. Now that the Children's Day holiday is approaching, a large-scale celebration should be held uniformly throughout the country. Therefore, it has specially submitted a presentation to the Municipal Government, requesting it to forward it to the National Government to promulgate a clear order as soon as possible and to request the Ministry of Interior and Education to jointly formulate implementation measures. The original presentation is recorded as follows:

Request to Promulgate a National Children's Year Case: This association previously, in order to arouse national attention to the promotion of children's welfare, suggested that the China Child Welfare Association present a request to the National Government to designate 1934 of the Republic of China as the National Children's Year. However, due to insufficient preparation, it was ordered to be held in 1935, while this city is still continuing to proceed separately with the will of Your Excellency. Now, it has been found that 1935 has already begun. Regarding the preparation for the National Children's Year, although it has been reported that the Ministry of Interior and Education have started planning, no clear order from the central government has been promulgated so far, causing the provinces and cities to wait and see and not know what to do. Even on the side of this city, although this association has jointly formed a National Children's Year Preparatory Committee with party and government agencies to preside over everything, it is unable to proceed due to the lack of an order from the central government. If it continues to be delayed, a year will easily pass and it will disappear invisibly, repeating the same mistakes as last year, which is contrary to the original intention of the government to promote children's welfare. In view of this, this association has submitted a resolution to the fifteenth standing committee meeting requesting Your Excellency to forward it to the National Government to promulgate this year as the National Children's Year as soon as possible and to designate Children's Day on April 4th as the opening date, ordering all provinces and cities to hold large-scale celebrations uniformly. It is reasonable to prepare a document and present it to Your Excellency for review and approval for forwarding, which is for the public convenience. Respectfully presented to Wu, Mayor of Shanghai, Pan Gongzhan, Standing Chairman of the Shanghai Children's Welfare Association.

Request to Formulate Children's Year Measures as Soon as Possible Case: This association previously, in order to arouse social attention to the promotion of children's welfare, specially suggested that the China Child Welfare Association present a request to the National Government to designate 1934 of the Republic of China as the National Children's Year. However, due to insufficient preparation, it was ordered to be postponed to 1935, while this city is still proceeding separately with the will of Your Excellency. Now, it has been found that 1935 has begun for more than a month. Although it has been reported that the implementation of the National Children's Year has been jointly prepared by the Ministry of Education and the Ministry of Interior, no concrete measures have been promulgated in clear orders so far. This association is deeply afraid that it will be delayed again and repeat the same mistakes as last year. Therefore, it dares to request Your Excellency to forward it to the Ministry of Education and the Ministry of Interior to quickly issue clear orders for the implementation measures of the National Children's Year in various provinces and cities, instructing them to comply. For the convenience of implementation in various provinces and cities, this association has also compiled and edited a book entitled "Implementation Methods of the Chinese Children's Year," which details the undertakings that should be carried out during the Children's Year and their methods, for the reference of various provinces and cities during implementation. In addition to sending it to the education bureaus of various provinces and cities, ten more copies are specially prepared and respectfully request that they be separately stored and forwarded to the Ministry of Education and the Ministry of Interior for review, ordering various provinces and cities to adopt them in order to broaden publicity and benefit the proceedings. Respectfully presented to Wu, Mayor of Shanghai, Pan Gongzhan, Standing Chairman of the Shanghai Children's Welfare Association.

General Evaluation Report of the National Labor Exhibition (2) 232

(1) The mowing machine, confluence pump, and vertical pump from Hubei Provincial Third Middle School. This school is an engineering-focused middle school, and it is commendable that it can manufacture such machinery. However, the workmanship is somewhat rough, and the materials are not very refined.

(2) The horse-powered water lifter, steam engine, hand-cranked water suction pump, and foot-operated water lifter from Jinan Junior Vocational School. The horse-powered water lifter has a clever design, but the workmanship is somewhat rough and should be improved. The same phenomenon applies to the other items. Students should be earnestly urged to strive for precision and quality materials to cultivate good habits.

(3) The vertical pump, four-foot single bed, pendulum pump, centrifugal dryer, and a set of wheel milling machines from Beijing Municipal Senior Vocational School. The pendulum pump and centrifugal dryer are well-made and very practical. However, the style of the lathe is somewhat old. Students' creative abilities should be earnestly guided in terms of design, and attention should be paid to accuracy during work.

(4) The 18-inch shaper, vertical drill press, and band saw from the Senior Industrial Vocational Department attached to the Hebei Provincial Institute of Technology. The machine forms are good, and the precision and materials are very sophisticated. It is rare for school products to be so excellent.

(5) The six-foot lathe, vertical drill press, hand-cranked drill press, and soap press from Baoding Senior Vocational School of Hebei Province. It is already not easy for vocational school students to manufacture such machinery. However, if students can pay close attention to the precision of research, the selection of materials, and the heat treatment of important steel parts, it will be even more perfect.

(6) The mechanical wood lathe, six-foot American-style lathe, bench lathe, rolling machine, small steam engine model, centrifugal suction pump, kerosene engine, circular saw, planer, and miscellaneous machine parts from the China Vocational School. The mechanical parts diagrams and implementations are displayed in comparison, which deeply reflects the intention of the exhibition and demonstrates the school's effective teaching. However, after examining the entire machine, it seems that the design of the mechanical wood lathe lacks robustness. Considering the excessive size of the tailstock screws and carriage of the six-foot American-style lathe, it is difficult to approach the headstock. If the hardness of the planer's blades and rollers can be increased, it will be more practical and durable. The circular saw and vertical drill press have excellent styles and exquisite workmanship, making them rare pieces of machinery.

(7) A set of screws and a set of pliers from the Second Vocational School of Hebei Province in Baoding, along with a complete set of parts and tools. It is very suitable to use small tools as teaching materials for schools. If steel materials can be selected and given appropriate hardness, and if large-scale manufacturing methods are promoted, it will be even more perfect.

(8) Gears, square screws, square anvils, calipers, scribers, and wrenches from Ningbo High School of Zhejiang Province. It is a special feature of the exhibition to have such works from high school students. Spring and Autumn

Odds and Ends 233

— (Reclining Buddha)

Some say: Youth is like a (spinning top), relying on their enthusiasm and courage, they are not afraid or slack in anything they do. When they reach middle age and gain a position of power based on their enthusiasm and courage, they transform into (abacus beads), only knowing how to calculate and seek advancement. By old age, enjoying their leisurely years and nurturing themselves in forests and springs, they no longer inquire about anything, becoming like (Buddha beads on a crown), merely ornamental. These three beads are a fitting portrayal of the Chinese people.

I often imagine this: the conscience of a traitor is utterly useless. If it could be extracted and implanted in the hearts of those who handle official matters, then those handling official matters, possessing a double dose of conscience, would surely achieve even better results. Similarly, bourgeois individuals always travel by boat or car, rendering their two feet completely useless. If those feet could be gifted to a group of lackeys, then with four feet, they would naturally be even more pleasing to their masters. There are many other such examples, but I cannot list them all. However, fantasies remain fantasies. Stubborn fate refuses to cooperate, so how can they be realized?

Superficial Talk 234

— Leanness and Refinement

Discussions of physiognomy are plentiful in ancient Chinese books and are hardly rare. During the Warring States period, there was a philosopher named Xunzi who advocated (rejecting physiognomy). (Gongsun Lü was said to have a face three feet long and three inches wide, yet his name moved the world.) Isn't that a bizarre appearance? I suspect there must be a typo. Perhaps (three feet) is a misprint of (one foot). Otherwise, even if such a visage existed thousands of years ago, wouldn't it terrify people? The Annals of Yanzi also state that (the face of Cheng Tang was rounded above and full below, and the face of Yi Yin was full above and rounded below.) According to this physiognomic interpretation, then Cheng Tang had a (由) character-shaped face, and Yi Yin had a (甲) character-shaped face. Simply by the size and shape of a person's face, their entire life's standing could be determined. Thus, the Zuo Zhuan records that (the inner historian Shu Fu said that Gu Ye's lower face was full, so he would surely have descendants in the state of Lu). The Guoyu also records that (Lu Shu Qiao Ru visited Zhou, and Wangsun Yue spoke with him, returning to tell King Jian that his appearance was square above and sharp below, suitable for offending people, and that the king should not reward him). The Book of Wei states that (Gu Bi's head was pointed, and Emperor Shizu jokingly called him "Pen Tip." At the time, everyone directly called him "Duke Pen"). The Biography of Li Anmin in the Book of Qi states that (Emperor Ming saw that Anmin threw five dice and all came up as "Lu," greatly alarming him. The Emperor said to Anmin, "Your face is as square as a field, a sign of being ennobled." (田) character-shaped face, now commonly called a square face, is perhaps the most perfect facial appearance in physiognomy. During the Three Kingdoms period, (Sun Quan had a square jaw and a large mouth.) It is said that his mouth could hold a fist, which his father Jian considered remarkable, deeming it an auspicious sign. That is the meaning!

In reality, in judging a person's face, skilled physiognomists always look for a rectangular shape, the so-called (同) character-shaped face, which is the most wealthy and noble configuration. If a person's outward appearance is roughly the same, but the cheekbones on either side are unusually prominent, then according to this diagram, it resembles the (風) character. Legal scholars say that prisoners who are imprisoned often have this appearance. There are also shapes like the (周) character, which is the worst of evil appearances because only one side protrudes, creating a malformed (周) character's (　). Look! Isn't that a monster? Therefore, scientists can use the angle of the facial bones to set standards when observing people's faces. People's intelligence is mostly uneven, but measuring their dimensions is accurate without the slightest error. The ancients said, (People's hearts are as different as their faces.) This is truly correct! In the book Gui Er Ji, (it is recorded) that the governor of a prefecture had a large and broad face, and he was posthumously named (西) character (face). It can be seen that facial features are not constant and ultimately not kind. Twenty years ago, someone inscribed Yuan Shikai's portrait with a (bear) face, Duan Qirui's portrait with a (swan) face, Huang Xing's portrait with a (pig) face, and Li Yuanhong's portrait with a (cow) face. They were not necessarily similar, but criticizing him was insulting to a great man, which was also unacceptable. Why? Comparing human faces to animal faces, those who have studied can always understand that Zhuge Jin of the Three Kingdoms had a (donkey) face, and Wei Ting of the Tang Dynasty had a (tiger) face, and there were even (monkey) faces and (dog) faces. If I were to list examples, humph! There are truly many!

Fire Alarm 235

— Wei Jing

In the still winter night air, the urgent sound of a siren suddenly transmitted. The sounds of people on the street also gradually changed from stillness to liveliness, and from liveliness to clamor.

The cries of (Fire | Fire | Fire |) were especially sent into the auditory organs of every person from the clamorous air. As a result, the residents of the entire street and the alleys on both sides hurriedly and frantically left their warm beds, rushing out to the door, shivering while inquiring where the fire was. Everyone's heart was filled with the hope that (the fire is still far away, it won't burn my house).

Thick white smoke violently spewed out from the doors and windows of a small grocery store at the entrance of the alley. The intense smell of burnt cloth filled the street and alley. The small grocery store, as well as the neighbors on either side of the small grocery store, were distraught, carrying out their boxes and belongings. The onlookers stared blankly. The hooligans were very active, trying to seize the opportunity to grab things. The police were maintaining order, waving their batons and hitting people indiscriminately. White smoke also began to rise from the roof of the small grocery store.

Amidst a tense wave of sound, the fire truck arrived. Firefighters wearing copper helmets jumped off the truck, connected the hose to the water hydrant, and the water drilled into the small grocery store like three giant snakes. In less than five minutes, the white smoke stopped seeping out from the gaps of the small grocery store. As a result, the sounds of people on the street gradually quieted down from the clamor.

The three giant python-like streams of water were still constantly drilling into the small grocery store. The crowd watching the excitement gradually dispersed, returning to their beds that had not yet cooled down to relive their good dreams.

The next day, anyone who passed by the door of the small grocery store would have to poke their head out to take a look at the remaining charred husk of the house. The boss with a round face deeply engraved with wrinkles, and the proprietress with a pair of very moving eyes, who knows where they have drifted.

— Tong Fu

Little Western Paradise 236

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter Eight: Remote Place, Carefree Officials Arrive with Strong-willed Mandates; Splendid Hall, Grand Banquet, Outside, Pitiable Creatures

A half-moon in the sky, in the deep blue night sky, sent some green light to the ground. At the corner of the wall, there were two shadows huddled together. At first, Jie Fu didn't pay much attention, seeing a thin stick tree, stretching half of it on the yellow soil wall, just this tree, shining in the moon, matched with the ancient roof, was another kind of flavor. Jie Fu, after all, had drunk a little ink, and suddenly the thought of home arose spontaneously. He recited Tang poetry loudly, saying; I pity my young children from afar, not understanding the longing for Chang'an. His poetic inspiration broke out, but it frightened the two people at the corner of the wall. With a "Oh," a person's shadow flashed, as if almost falling down. Jie Fu then understood that there were two women. Like Little Western Paradise, every time it reached this beginning of nightfall, there was a batch of pitiful women, looking for a temporary way out here. Naturally, there were also those who knew that eating was important, and that shame was not unnecessary, so they did not dare to blatantly look for guests, but secretly hid and flashed, waiting for the waiter to come out and pass on the message. Zhang Jie Fu guessed that they were also this kind of people, and laughed: This is not worth being startled, wow. Who are you waiting for here? I'll send a message to him and let him come out. It's also very cold under the moon, don't catch a cold. As he said this, his footsteps kept moving over. In his heart, he thought that these women were nothing, and it was something the guests of Little Western Paradise couldn't get enough of when speaking with them. But as he moved forward, the two women leaned against the wall, slowly retreating backward. Jie Fu laughed: Aren't you looking for guests of Little Western Paradise? I am too. Why..." He said, already very close, and he could see clearly that the woman in front was Zhu Yueying, and the one behind had a bun on her head. Only then did he feel rash, how could he joke with people like this. (One Two Eight)

Scented Imperial Records 237

— Original work by Princess Der Ling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

As for the reason for the discord between Empress Jiashun and Empress Dowager Cixi, it is recorded very clearly in Hu Sijing's "Guowen Beicheng." One passage says: (The establishment of Empress Yi (i.e., Jiashun) was decided by Empress Dowager Ci'an, not by Xiaoqin (i.e., Cixi). After Ci'an's death, Xiaoqin became even more fond of Concubine Hui (the concubine was the daughter of Fengxiu; Cixi wanted to establish her when Tongzhi selected his consort but was unsuccessful). She instructed the emperor to treat her with extra courtesy and not to visit the central palace often. Emperor Muzong (i.e., Tongzhi) heavily defied the wishes of both empress dowagers, always sleeping alone in the palace, feeling depressed and unhappy. Evil people then tempted him to visit the people. The empress once wrote the two characters (戒嬉), "admonish against frivolity," and posted them in the corner of her seat to advise Muzong, which was known throughout the country as her virtue. When Muzong was on the verge of death, the empress entered the palace to inquire about his illness, but Xiaoqin resented that she had not reported to her first, severely reprimanding her. The empress angrily said, (I entered through the Great Qing Gate in a phoenix-drawn chariot, which the whole world knows. Now I enter the palace to inquire about the emperor's illness. What crime have I committed to be questioned by the empress dowager?)! Xiaoqin suspected that the empress was intentionally criticizing her, and she loudly rebuked her, saying: "You wench, do you think I have never entered the Great Qing Gate? You entered through me; how do you know you won't exit through me!)! When Muzong died, she did not establish an heir for him, forcing her to commit suicide.) This passage is generally reliable. Therefore, it is specially extracted so that readers, after reading it and then reading the following text, will not be without a clue.)

(The suffering we endured is truly beyond words!) The Empress Dowager continued, (Because of the matter of propriety, we had to endure until she herself sought a short death. Only then did we feel relieved as if we had seen the light of day again!)

That's right, everyone knows that the death of Empress Tongzhi was indeed a suicide, so the Empress Dowager herself believed that there was no need to hide it any further. Furthermore, I also heard people say that because the Empress Dowager was usually dissatisfied with Empress Tongzhi, she deliberately satirized her after Tongzhi's death, saying that a truly virtuous wife should have died with her husband and should not have lived on. As a result, Empress Tongzhi could not help but die. (Translator's note: Cixi forced Empress Xiaozhe to die with all her might, not just with cold irony and sarcasm. Fei Xingjian (Cixi's Biography True Record) records it in detail. The general idea is: Cixi once publicly humiliated Xiaozhe at the funeral and even slapped her face. The empress left, and that night, she hanged herself.) (Two Three Eight)

Echoes of Lamentation 238

— (Cheng Zhenru)

After reading Jiao Xin Jun's (Vegetable Prices After the Famine), a scene of profound tragedy replayed in my mind. One year of hard work, a year of famine inevitably leads to escape. I will record below what I felt and wrote in my diary a month ago. This is the voice of the Liyang farmers, perhaps it can supplement the Spring and Autumn Annals?

Spreading fertilizer and applying fertilizer is labor in vain,

Two hundred and eighty for one hundred pounds of green vegetables,

Four pounds of salt for one hundred pounds of green vegetables,

Six hundred copper coins with one string of cash.

Wherever my travels reach

A Lone Visit to the Fragrant Sea Pavilion at Chao Mountain 239

— Wang Fang'an

Not many days ago, at the home of Wu Changshuo's son, Dong Mai, in Jiqing Lane, North Shanxi Road, I unexpectedly encountered the abbot of Bao Ci Temple from Chao Mountain, the Venerable Guang Zhou. He told me that the Fragrant Sea Pavilion, which had been destroyed by fire, had recently been completed, thanks to Mr. Xi Guansheng of Panyu's fundraising and labor. It was finished just before the plum blossoms and snow began to compete for spring. The next morning, I met Venerable Guang Zhou again at Mr. Yao Chuqin's residence. He said that because of the mild weather these past few days, the faint fragrance from the branches near the water's edge would soon be wafting in the air. This piqued my interest in exploring the plum blossoms at Chao Mountain.

That day happened to be a Sunday holiday. I boarded the Shanghai-Hangzhou train at the North Station at 9:15 in the morning. Around 2 PM, the train delivered me to Linping. I jumped off the train and walked to the bus station on Hangtang Road.

The bus on Hangtang Road took me to Chao Mountain in less than twenty minutes. This was a familiar path to me. I entered Turtle Mountain West Village and climbed the mountainside of Snake Mountain. Along the way, I listened to the strangely pleasant local accent. Before I knew it, I had arrived at the Song Plum Pavilion.

In front of Bao Ci Temple, beside the Song Plum Pavilion, it was very quiet and desolate. There were no other tourists and no villagers. The Fragrant Sea Pavilion had indeed been restored to its former appearance, and it seemed even more solemn and serene than before. I wandered alone for a long time. The Song Plum, with its old branches stretching sideways, having endured all kinds of weather, was like an old monk in meditation, not even the branches moving. Looking closely through the fence, I could indeed see a few six-petaled flowers blooming on the branches. The flower buds, waiting to open, were scattered like stars. The newly transplanted old plum tree opposite seemed even more flourishing. A faint breeze occasionally carried a hint of fragrance. I imagined that at dusk when the moon rose, the scene would be even more enchanting.

I stepped into the lower level of the Fragrant Sea Pavilion and spent a lot of time climbing the stairs and gazing into the distance. I couldn't help but recall my long-held wish to point at the peaks and buy a mountain to live in seclusion. Turning back, I saw that the east wing of Bao Ci Temple, which had been destroyed, had also been restored to its former appearance. Who could say that this wasn't Venerable Guang Zhou's grand aspiration come true?

However, Venerable Guang Zhou had not yet returned to the mountain. I was too lazy to deal with the guest master at the temple. In the twilight, I bid farewell to the Fragrant Sea Pavilion and boarded the last bus on Hangtang Road, staying overnight in my hometown.

The next morning, I returned to Shanghai. I passed by Chao Mountain again along the way, but the beautiful scene flashed by in an instant!

Commercial News

Cotton Yarn Sales in Shanghai for the Third Year of the Republic 240

Total Sales Amounted to 319,923 Bales

An Increase of 82,732 Bales Compared to the Previous Year

Attached: Comparative Table of Monthly High and Low Prices of Cotton Yarn

According to the actual sales of spot cotton yarn in the twenty-third year of the Republic, the total sales volume for the entire year was 319,923 bales, an increase of 82,732 bales compared to the 237,191 bales of the previous year. The reason for the increase is attributed to Japanese merchants being unwilling to cut prices and dump yarn, believing that the situation in North China was stable. Therefore, around June and July, the prices of Chinese yarn were particularly cheap in the north. The Tianjin, Gaoyang, Weihaiwei, North China, and Henan groups saw a large increase in the sales of coarse yarn, mostly 10-count and 17-count yarn. Tianjin's total transaction volume for the year was 28,803 bales, a large increase of 28,473 bales compared to the previous 330 bales. The North China group's total transaction volume was 10,725 bales, an increase of 9,510 bales compared to the previous year's 1,221 bales. Henan's transaction volume was 12,873 bales, with no transactions in the previous year. The Southern Guangdong and Yunnan groups saw an increase in sales due to lower prices. Guangdong's total transaction volume for the year was 64,881 bales, an increase of 17,706 bales compared to the previous year's 47,174 bales. Yunnan's transaction volume was 26,572 bales, an increase of 6,795 bales compared to the previous year's 19,777 bales. The inland's total transaction volume for the year was 74,455 bales, a large increase of 28,553 bales compared to the previous year's 45,902 bales. Hunan and Jiangxi saw a slight increase in sales due to the victory in bandit suppression. However, Sichuan was severely affected by rampant banditry, with exchange rates soaring to 1,500 yuan, greatly impacting yarn sales. Not only did sales not increase, but they actually decreased significantly. The total transaction volume for the year was only 24,993 bales, a large decrease of 17,944 bales compared to the previous year's 42,937 bales. The transaction volume for January was 17,636 bales, February was 11,390 bales, March was 13,680 bales, April was 26,376 bales, May was 37,235 bales, June was 23,166 bales, July was 26,056 bales, August was 32,350 bales, September was 35,858 bales, and October (the peak transaction month) saw increased activity by customer groups due to news of increased consolidated taxes from the Ministry of Finance, with 40,681 bales. American Cotton Market in Stagnation Pending Resolution of Gold Bar Embezzlement Case 241

Yesterday, the American cotton market opened with quiet trading and prices down 1-2 points. Subsequently, due to unfavorable news from Liverpool, some long positions were liquidated and foreign merchants sold, causing prices to continue to decline. Midway, due to limited selling, fellow traders bought in, resulting in a slight rebound. However, the stock market remained sluggish and local traders sold, preventing any significant improvement. At the close, short covering led to a relatively stable situation. Spot prices were down 5 points, while futures prices for all months except October were down 2-5 points. Currently, cotton markets across the United States are in a state of stagnation, awaiting the resolution of the gold bar embezzlement case. The British cotton market was weak due to selling from Bombay traders, with spot prices down 3 points and futures unchanged. The Indian cotton market initially strengthened due to buying from European exporters and Japanese merchants, but later retreated due to the liquidation of large long positions. Phalgool was down 1.5 rupees, Oomra was down 2 rupees, and Broach was down 0.75 rupees. The original telegram is recorded on the left (dated the 29th).

Financial News: British and American Exchange Rates Drop Sharply 242

Gold Market and Chinese Banks Still Closed for Holiday

Western Merchants Lack Spot Silver, Forcing Down Forward Prices

Dalian Banks Sell Off Gold Futures Contracts at Lower Prices in the Black Market

According to yesterday's foreign dispatches, London spot and forward prices both fell by 1/8, New York silver prices also dropped by 1/8, and forward silver prices in Montreal fell by varying amounts of 2.5 to 3.5 percent. London pure gold fell by 3 pence, British pounds versus US dollars unchanged, US dollars versus British pounds rose by 0.25, British pounds versus French francs rose by 3 pounds, US dollars versus French francs unchanged. At the morning opening, the recent selling price for British exchange was 1 shilling, 5 pence, and 3/8 (0.375), and for American exchange was 35.375 yuan, which was tighter by 0.0625 for British and 0.125 for American compared to the previous close. However, immediately after opening, the market strengthened. The Central Bank's official rate announcement showed a tightening of 0.125 for British and 0.1875 for American exchange. The customs gold unit rose by 0.011 (yuan). Although Cheng Feng Yong and others were buying, the banks' supply had little impact. The HSBC announced its official rate with both British and American exchanges unchanged. Later, Sassoon began selling spot shillings, and thereafter banks suddenly started large-scale selling, causing the market to strengthen further. Although the silver equalization tax remained unchanged, foreign banks lacked spot silver and Chinese banks were still closed for the holiday, while the gold market was also closed. As a result, there was a lack of support, and spot prices were driven up while forward prices weakened. The domestic market repeatedly loosened, and even though the Jewish merchant, George Joe, came to buy, the banks' selling interest was still strong, and the situation at noon remained unfavorable. Although the American Eastern Bank took delivery, it had no impact, and the afternoon market remained strong. The initial Indian silver price rose by 7.3 annas, but after entering the market, banks began to sell again, while the Dalian Savings Company also took delivery, resulting in a flat market. Although the second Indian silver price rose by 3.1 annas, it slightly softened in the end. The closing selling prices for recent contracts were 1 shilling, 5 pence, and 13/16 (0.8125) for British exchange and 36.25 yuan for American exchange, which was looser by 0.375 for British and tighter by 0.6875 for American compared to the previous close. Some Chinese merchants, such as Cheng Feng Yong and Sheng Da, were buying slightly, while the Dalian banks and savings companies sold off gold futures contracts, with black market prices ranging from around 958 to 951 yuan, eventually settling above 3 yuan. After Resolution of the US Gold Bar Case Regarding Silk and Tea 244

Domestic and Foreign Sales of Raw Silk Will Inevitably Increase

According to reports, the US gold bar case will be postponed until February 12th for sentencing. Currently, the atmosphere in New York's financial and industrial sectors remains turbulent, and the outlook for the silk market is difficult to predict. Therefore, the Shanghai market situation remains sluggish. However, according to a Westerner, the verdict of the gold bar case, regardless of who wins or loses, is irrelevant. He only hopes for a quick resolution to dispel the lingering wait-and-see attitude in the market, allowing various transactions to become as active as before. Whether the government wins the case, its financial position will be strengthened, and the industrial sector can be at ease in their respective businesses. Conversely, the wise US government will surely have other effective ways to recover its losses. Some people say that there will be market turmoil after the verdict, but he said this is not credible. By then, the sluggish market atmosphere will have dissipated, and spring sales of raw silk both domestically and abroad will inevitably increase. Given the imbalance between supply and demand in the Chinese silk market, market prices may see an improvement as a result.

Free Talk

Problems Concerning the Relationship Between Literature and Science 251

— Xin Ren

I have already said a few words about this issue, but because someone has misinterpreted them, I am bringing it up again for discussion.

The presentation and resolution of every issue cannot be separated from concrete reality. Furthermore, in the process of presenting and resolving the issue, the main thing is to make the opinions more systematic. Blindly pulling and tugging is of no use. Regarding this issue, I believe that it should be presented and resolved from two aspects. One aspect is essential, elucidating the similarities and differences between literature (art) and science, and thus inferring what kind of relationship the two should have. The other aspect is more concrete, paying attention to the current situation in China and proposing how to realize the aforementioned relationship. By science, I mean both social science and natural science.

The first problem arises because people have always only noticed the differences between literature (art) and science, neglecting their similarities. That is, they only notice that art is emotional and science is rational, and therefore think that the two are unrelated or incompatible. They do not know that art, literature, and science are all powerful tools for humans to understand and transform reality, and all reflect the development of reality. Although artists and scientists each have different ways of expressing reality, in understanding reality, they have closely related and consistent methods (epistemology and its methodology). Therefore, here we find the essential basis for literature (art) to be closely linked with science. In the past, naturalistic writers used natural science to create artistic works, but they did not have the correct methods. As a result, although they obtained some excellent results, they also brought about huge failures, because they could not accurately understand the qualitative differences between human society and the natural world. They did not understand that (humans) are the sum total of social relationships, and only described them as animals in a gregarious setting. In the recent past and present, another group of writers simply applied the principles of social science to literature, fragmenting reality to fit into their narrow abstract concepts. As a result, they created a large pile of novel formulas, poetry formulas, and so on. Needless to say, this was caused by the incorrect grasp of creative methods. At the same time, we can also draw an important conclusion here, that the true (cooperation) between science (social science and natural science) and literature (art) absolutely does not mean the accumulation of academic knowledge, but rather means cooperation in understanding reality. That is to say, literature and science can only achieve a true sense of integration in the process of practice. Balzac received the (Social Science Doctorate) honor because he closely linked literature and science within a certain practical limit. Goethe, who was rich in natural science knowledge, had long said: (You can't know anything by just studying, you always need the necessity of practice.) The above words are my essential opinions on the mutual (penetration) of literature and science. Some people think that it is superfluous to propose this opinion, because it (seems to have been explained thoroughly enough in the past). However, I think this is necessary to prevent the essential meaning of the (mutual penetration) of literature and science from being ignored. If this meaning is neglected, true results cannot be obtained smoothly. And in fact, those who claim to be (thorough enough) are often not (thorough) at all. For example, (literature is the lower base of ideology), (literature is a department of social science) (both seen in this column on January 15), words like these may barely gain a seat when (odd articles are shared), but using ordinary (old sayings) to say it, it is (nonsense), and fundamentally does not understand what literature and science are and the essential meaning of their interrelationship.

The second question stems from the first question. Due to the obstacles of the private social system, literature and science have always been the exclusive property of a few people, and have never achieved true unity. Now that we have affirmed the important relationship between literature and science above, we should try to universalize both. Let me add a word here, limiting science solely to natural science, especially at the current stage, is completely failing to understand the true meaning of the mutual (penetration) of literature and science. This essentially ignores the importance of social science to China at the present stage. In his article (On Scientific Essays), Mr. Liu Shizhi gave many concrete explanations of this (penetration) problem. Now, essays have not only married science, but also given birth to sons. This trend can develop into the combination of literary science. I believe that in the near future, we will see works like Ilyin's (The Story of the Five-Year Plan), because this kind of work has its important social necessity at the current stage. In the process of promoting the true connection between literature and science, universalization or popularization is the most important and only means, but we cannot simply regard this as the entire meaning of the whole problem, and think that (the penetration of natural science and literature is not a matter of method, but a matter of the reason for the subject matter.) Because universalization is the (reasoning) method of the problem at the current stage, and it is also a matter of cultural education.

Discussing Poetry is Like Discussing Zen 252

— Xiao Wu

Poets often attribute the world to their own subjective views, and express their desires and emotions in life, forming the content of poetry. Although there may be various different schools in style, such as simplicity, elegance, sadness, and heroism, the pure Platonic thought and sentiment, as well as the expressed Passion, are the same. The poet's thought is philosophical, not belonging to the world of Aristotle, so in poetry there is often hidden a philosophical concept, a Zen machine. Reading ancient poems, we often sigh and ponder, like chewing olives, and this is why. For example, when we read:

(Sad falling leaves, fluttering down in layers. Layers. Layers fall and fly, going horizontally and never returning. The long shade of intertwined branches was once so dense? The yellow birds sing and lose each other. Evening medicine mixes with condensed frost, morning falls and turns to fly in the sun, chaotic spring sun, rises spring breeze, spring breeze and spring sun are the same at this time. One frost and two frosts can still be endured, five mornings and six days have already withered yellow. Suddenly, a gust of wind lifts them, soaring high and low. Sad falling leaves, when will the falling leaves return? They shared the same root in the past, but now they have no connection, each following the dust and dirt, and it is difficult to climb the high branches again. —Xiao Zong of the Northern Wei Dynasty, "Sad Falling Leaves.")

We can know that this is not only a work of Shu Zhi when Xiao Zong was frustrated, but also contains a philosophical exploration of life for one's own subjective purposes. This kind of subtle and distant Zen machine is hidden between chanting and sighing, and cannot be excavated. This sense of subtlety and distance that cannot be excavated is precisely the valuable part of poetry. Throughout history, there have been no shortage of great theorists of poetry. Although their arguments are not consistent, they seem to agree on focusing on (grasping the infinite).

In my opinion, the greatest theorist of poetry who thoroughly implemented this meaning throughout history was Yan Yu of the Song Dynasty. Yan Yu's Canglang Poetry Talk says: (Discussing poetry is like discussing Zen. The poetry of the Han, Wei, Jin, and High Tang dynasties is the first meaning; the poetry since the Dali era is small vehicle Zen. The poetry of the Late Tang Dynasty is the sound-heard Pratyekabuddha fruit. The masters of the High Tang Dynasty only focus on interest, like a antelope hanging its horns, with no trace to be found. Therefore, its subtlety is transparent and exquisite, impossible to approach, like sound in the air, color in appearance, the moon in the well, the image in the mirror, words are finite and meaning is infinite. Modern gentlemen make strange explanations, and then take words as poetry, talent as poetry, and discussion as poetry. How can they not be skillful, but they are ultimately not our poetry. For in the sound of chanting and sighing, there is a sense of regret.)

In this passage, he advocates that poetry should be like (sound in the air), (color in appearance), (the moon in the well), (the image in the mirror), which is the so-called pure Platonic thought and sentiment as well as the form of the expressed Passion. He opposes (taking words as poetry), (taking talent as poetry), and even (taking discussion as poetry). This kind of view is not only worthy of attention at that time, but also has its value when applied to modern times. We know that there are more people doing poetry of the kinds that Yan Yu would have opposed than can be counted. Among them, there are certainly those who play games with words, and it cannot be said that there are absolutely no people who flaunt their talents, and as for the great poets who claim to lead the masses and only know how to (make arguments), they are even too numerous to count. The greatest achievement of these kinds of poets is probably nothing more than oppressing the Muse with brute force and making the poetry scene deserted.

Speaking of this, I have not forgotten to tell people not to be (poetry artisans). In other words, although the vernacular poems of Wang Fanzhi (Hanshan, Shide, Shao Yong) are rich in Zen, it is not appropriate to regard them as supreme treasures. Muddled-headed games should be respectfully avoided from the greatest differences.

The Celebrated Jumping Frog (Part 2) 253

— Written by Mark Twain, Translated by Libo

Xi Xie Smilu had a mare—the children called her the Fifteen-Minute Mare, but, you know, that was just a joke. Naturally, she was faster than that—and he often won money on that mare, even though she was so slow, and often wheezed, was dizzy, had lung disease, or some other similar ailment. They always gave her two or three hundred yards, always passing her halfway through, but in the final, difficult stretch of the race, she would get very excited, looking like she was trying her hardest, jumping, her legs kicking wildly in the harness, sometimes high in the air, sometimes stepping on the garden walls, kicking up more and more dust. Her choking, sneezing, snorting, caused more and more clamor—you could see that he always reached the finish line a neck ahead.

He had a small, fierce dog. Looking at him, it seemed he wasn't worth a cent, except to lie there honestly, waiting for a chance to steal something. But when money was bet on him, he was different; his jaw began to protrude, like the forecastle of a steamer, and his teeth would glow like a stove. Another dog would tease him, threaten him, bite him, and even throw him over his shoulder two or three times. Andre Mackson—that was the dog's name—Andre Jackson wouldn't pretend, he was just content, he wouldn't hope for anything else—the bets on the opponent were doubled and redoubled until all the money was gone; then, suddenly, he would seize the other dog's hind leg, right at the joint, biting tightly—not tearing, you understand, just holding on tightly, until they called a truce, even if it took a year. Smilu always won betting on that little dog, until he tangled with a dog that had no hind legs, because that dog's hind legs had been sawn off with a circular saw. When the time was ripe, and all the money was bet, he went straight for that cherished leg joint. He immediately saw how he had been tricked, how he had fallen into the dog cage. He looked surprised, and soon he was very depressed, and he didn't want to fight this battle anymore. He was very agitated. He looked at Smilu as if to say his heart was broken, and it was all his fault, he didn't refuse to fight a dog without hind legs to seize, and seizing hind legs was his main reliance in battle. So he walked a few steps weakly, and lay down and died. That was a good little dog, that Andre Jackson, and if he were still alive, he would be famous, because he had that foundation, and he had talent—I know, if he didn't have talent, he would never have had the chance to be talked about, and his ability to fight like that in that environment is inexplicable. I always feel sad when I think of his last battle and its outcome.

My Factory Trip 254

— Li Qiao

Every year in the first and second months of the lunar calendar, in the misty mornings when the sun was just beginning to rise, groups of people, carrying small bundles and wearing tattered bamboo hats, their faces etched with the bitter sorrow of departure, would march out of the east gate of their hometown like a crusading expedition, heading to Gejiu, more than three hundred miles away, to work in the tin mines.

These people who went to work in the mines were mostly bankrupt farmers and unemployed individuals. When they left in the spring, they mostly looked like impoverished refugees. But when they returned at the end of the lunar year, it was a completely different story: they wore brand-new blue coarse cloth clothes, a small melon-shaped hat with a red knot on their heads, their clothes were half-open, their peach-red faces carried a hint of newfound wealth and pride, and they were even healthier than before. Seeing acquaintances, they were always smiling, as if they had done something triumphant. That sight always made me very envious!

Perhaps it was also because all my friends who used to hang out together had gone out, leaving me alone at home tilling the fields, which felt too monotonous? So I also wanted to go to work in the mines!

But this idea was always rejected by my father, who wore a bitter expression:

(I'm over fifty years old, what haven't I done? Work in the mines, do you think it's so easy? I used to work in the mines for many years—what good is it? I've said before: I won't even look at the Gejiu mines when I'm urinating or defecating, and you still want to go?)

My father was furious, and spittle flew from his toothless mouth. I knew what he meant. He hoped that I would be like him, honestly tilling the land for the rest of my life, and not have any extravagant illusions, because he had been through it all, he had tasted all the suffering in the world, and knew how fate was determined. But I, being stubborn, always refused to listen to my father. My heart had already been taken to Gejiu by those proud people who returned from Gejiu every year with their wealth. I wanted to go to that place of wealth—Gejiu!

So, I continued to idealize Gejiu. I imagined myself as a future boss, who would return on a magnificent horse when I became rich. At that time, my hard-working parents would no longer have to suffer other people's anger, and be tenants for others. At that time, we would build our own house, and no longer live in that broken earthen hut... These ideals strengthened my resolve without me realizing it. Although my father had told me what kind of place it was, and how dangerous it was, and that it was very easy to die in the mines at any time... I still insisted on going!

This stubborn determination left my father helpless. But in his heart, he thought that I was still so young, and even though I said I wanted to go, would I really go?

This was something they did not expect: one morning, when the golden sunlight had just kissed the roof ridge, while they were busy working and not paying attention, I quietly stole a tattered bamboo hat and followed an acquaintance who was going to Gejiu (to transport water) and slipped out of the house.

This was truly something no one knew. Tiptoeing behind him, all the way until we were about to get on the boat, the water carrier turned around and saw me, and, surprised, quickly put down his load, and said in an unusual tone:

(Ah, where are you going?)

(Gejiu!)

(You're going to work in the mines too?) The water carrier looked at me, so young and laughable, and couldn't help but laugh, mockingly saying to me: (Is all you need to work in the mines just this tattered bamboo hat?)

I was ashamed and didn't say anything. He came closer and grabbed me: (Go back, go back! ...You're still too young. Wait until you're older next year and then go...).

(No, I want to go this year!)

(Hey, is that a place for you to go?)

As he spoke, regardless of whether I cried or not, he tightly pinched my arm and sent me home like he was pulling a criminal.

This setback made me very sad. But the following year, under the pressure of merciless life, no one stopped me anymore, letting an ignorant eleven- or twelve-year-old child leave his hometown alone to a strange place, to taste the first bitter cup of life.

— TK

Small Pleasure Boat 256

— Zheng Zhaojia

In the winter, the setting sun slants into the deep purple mountain peaks. The young masters in the villages, who are already accustomed to a materialistic lifestyle, take out their pocket watches to check the time. They secretly stuff large amounts of money into their silk pockets, and hurry out of their own house gates, heading to the small pleasure boats moored beside the small river.

In that secluded place, not far from the village, three or four pleasure boats are moored. Inside the boats, there are songs and laughter. In the evening, the calm river surface gradually becomes agitated, stirring up endless joy and troubles for people.

The wealthy and amorous young men in the village secretly gather there, and in the midst of wild drinking and laughter, they all seem to lose their senses, forgetting the old master's intimidating beard at home, forgetting the old mother's red eyes, explaining everything to her husband on behalf of her son, and even forgetting their own moments of repentance, immersing themselves in the embrace of the pleasure girls.

The pleasure girls help the drunk guests into the back cabin. The guests hold the boat girls in their arms and drag them to a wooden bed covered with a mat, doing all sorts of different things. The boat girls don't show any impatience. Experience tells them that wealthy young masters have big tempers and are not easy to provoke. If they are served well, they will be rewarded generously.

When dusk arrives, that group of delirious people returns. Those who are drunk as mud are awakened with cold water by the boat girls. They stagger back into their own house gates and run back to their own rooms, forgetting the cold. Their minds are as if filled with mercury, dazed and confused. The old master's intimidating beard and the old mother's red eyes gradually creep back into their memories. Fortunately, there is only one such joyous occasion a year. They forgive themselves in this way, but after climbing into bed, they cannot sleep all night, tempted by the boat girl's slender figure and full, fleshy body! In the evening, the pleasure boats change to another group of people. Young, unmarried farmers, all holding boundless hopes, also sneak into the cabins, having all drunk old wine at home. They are preparing to spend a sweet winter night here.

The boat girls send away those young masters, because it is very dangerous to let a young master from a wealthy family spend the night on their boat. If the young masters' family finds them on their boat, that's not a joke. Not only will their boat be confiscated by the county, but they will also be severely beaten by the boat boss, because the wealthy old masters from those families have great influence and reputation. If they know that their sons have done such a thing, it would be terrible. Therefore, they investigate the guests who want to stay overnight in great detail. Because the farmers have no power and no reputation, the boat girls sleep with them in peace.

The pleasure boats spend the winter by the small river in the village. In the spring, they don't do business according to their rules, but sail elsewhere. They dock here again next winter. The pleasure girls on the boats are of course replaced with new ones, but they become more fashionable every year. Therefore, the new styles of women in the city are also brought to this lonely village every year.

Every year after the pleasure boats sail elsewhere, in the garbage dumps by the small river, one can see what they have left behind: a bloody thing wrapped in straw and mats, which are the premature babies born to the pleasure girls. When the river water rises to the beach in the spring, those things born to the pleasure girls are also washed away to other places along with the river water.

However, in recent years, the secluded small river where the pleasure boats used to dock has been replaced by two or three bandit ships in the winter.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Random Talk

On Adapting to the Environment 257

— Rong

According to biologists, all living things must adapt to their environment in order to survive. Even the green color of a small insect is to adapt to the green of the grass, in order to avoid being captured. As for humans, of course, they are no exception. However, since humans are known as the spirit of all things, they have more sophisticated skills and means to adapt to the more complex environment. We usually work day and night, living a common life like millions of others, but sometimes, the individual's will conflicts with the surrounding environment, and this is when a tragedy unfolds. Bergson said: We usually have two personalities, one is peaceful, retiring, and conservative, and the other is violent, reckless, and destructive. The former appears in our daily interactions, while the latter appears when the individual conflicts with society. If we examine ourselves, this is certainly not without reason. When grief and anger arise, one truly feels that although the world is vast, there is no place for oneself, or one looks around and feels that there is no one to talk to. Here, the lesson of adapting to the environment is needed.

Humans are inherently social animals, and cannot live a solitary life like Robinson Crusoe. All the people in society are closely related to oneself. In the past, many poets who claimed to be lonely said that they existed awake amidst the drunkenness of the masses, but they could not leave this so-called (drunken) society, could they? This is really comical upon careful thought. On the one hand, one hates the people around them, and on the other hand, one cannot truly isolate oneself from these people. As a result, one either loses others or others lose oneself. The ends of both paths are tragedy. Since we know that individualism is just a deformed attitude to life, since we know that human nature contains an innate sense of sociability, since we know that we cannot force society to follow oneself, then why not change our attitude, correct our own aloofness, and adapt to this society and improve this society? A passive attitude is not a good example to follow. It not only does not benefit society, but also makes one's own survival a problem. Complaining, being angry, and resisting will only result in irrational madness and be ridiculed by people as a fool. To put it bluntly, this is selling one's life cheaply!

Of course, we cannot deny that pure young people are often appalled by the dark and evil aspects of society. It is certainly uncomfortable at first to spend all day with people who eat meat and laugh, or to say "Nice weather today! Ha!!" when they meet, or to indulge in wine and mahjong. But over time, habit becomes second nature, and one gradually drowns in the murky current. Especially in our moderate, lukewarm, and viscous nation, within a few years, an energetic young person will be molded by the environment to be polite and restrained, with no fire, becoming the person they once hated. Adapting to such an environment is not easy!

But should we therefore escape? Society is treacherous, and life is rugged. Since we are born as human beings, we bear the responsibility of pioneering the way through hardship. I believe that the environment is a large crucible. Only by tempering oneself in it can one develop one's personality. As for those who adapt to the environment, they are simply those who are not reckless or evasive in their dealings with the world. The motto of the ancient philosophers is (Harmony without Uniformity)!

A Stroll in the Desert 258

— Xu Xizhen

(I hear that the dreams of those who travel in the remote African deserts every night are of the beautiful mountains and rivers of their homeland.

— Kume Masamura: Symbol of Anguish)

Also) At night, I dreamed of the beautiful hometown of my childhood, like a mythical fairy island.

(There, a mist-like poetic haze permeates—the mist carries the breath of the morning.

And so: every spring, the wild roses on the short fence in front of my house bloom, and the grapevines spread verdantly and windingly to endless lengths: from here, a trace of gentle emotion is read. The moon, night after night, presents itself with the appearance of an ancient mirror, illuminating the tranquility of this small village, illuminating all kinds of bright little dreams, illuminating much of the frankness of childhood. The water in the small stream flows like the floating of clouds, with boundless joy in its simplicity—it is the original form of the human world, and also the symphony of the bright melody of the flow of life.

One morning, one evening, people are accompanied by the low and quiet bell sounds of the small temple, tranquil and far-reaching: and so: like the stubbornness of an old goat, they fall into deep thought—people think about a star, a petal, a drop of stream water, a seed, a light cloud.

Worries? Terror? Torment? Hurt?

The terribleness of the human world is non-existent—perhaps they are hidden in an unknowable stratum.

The human world is eternally beautiful, like a cluster of fireworks.)

However, when I wake up, I realize once again: I have been deceived once more—deceived by a dream!

I am traveling alone in the African desert of the human world—an endless desert.

The land is barren, a thousand miles, ten thousand miles, without green grass or moist water droplets. Dirty sand flies in the wind, blinding people's eyes and suffocating their breath—in the desert, even the sun is seen as malicious and cruel.

Right? The desert has no boundaries. Lying in front of people is a vast expanse of sand: travelers walk and walk, but finally cannot help but begin to doubt what the journey in this desert itself represents.

To say that it is seeking a miracle in the human world; but who can believe such an implausible statement? — The wasteland of life is not comfortable like velvet — on the contrary, isn't it clearly filled with witheredness, dryness, harshness, and a thousand kinds of exploitative natural phenomena? What the traveler thrown into the desert asks for is not the glittering splendor of luxury, but some ordinary products of nature: a blade of green grass, a milky white lily, a dewdrop, a breath of moist air.

However, those who have been exiled to the wasteland of life are not allowed even this little hope.

Youth in the desert is like the salty, light breeze on the sea: and so, traces are carved on the traveler's face: they are old, but why do they still have to carry heavy luggage, pick up a dead branch as a cane, and limp step by step, never stopping?

To say that life has a legendary beauty is perhaps clever; however, the shadow etched in the heart of the traveler in the desert does not allow for any defense.

In this way, I will begin to learn to endure a more desolate state of mind from today onwards. When I know that I must remain in the desert for the rest of my life, why bother to remember the beauty of another world?

(The dreams of those who travel in the African desert every night are of the beautiful mountains and rivers of their homeland!)

But today, even this beautiful dream has disappeared.

A Handbook for the Lonely 259

— Luo Jia

Walking along the coal cinder road, the rows of holly trees lining the road, the December wind, is obviously brash. After being sick, my pace is a little bit sluggish.

The roots of a wax plum tree are just enough to make a seat for me. The rich fragrance of the wax plum is more intoxicating than mixed wine. I cannot bear such a nearly oppressive temptation. My throat itches, I am almost vomiting. Yes! I want to be quiet, I want to be detached. Anything that is too rich, too extravagant, too glorious is despised by me.

X X X X

Cigarettes are my best friend. At dusk, the room is dark, the light is not on. Kissing its pure white body, sitting in a velvet-faced recliner, my thoughts are clear, clearer than the clear sky in autumn. There is not a trace of impurities here, and this is when I am at my most intelligent.

Afterward, I fall into inescapable error. Prejudice ferments in my heart. So, I despise women. Should women be slaves to sex? In order to show the greatness of their sexual instincts, they fully expose all their seductive powers, hoping that some stupid men, wanting to get a moment of pleasure, will willingly be used by them. This fully demonstrates their selfish desires and vulgar aspirations.

Therefore, I despise women.

X X X

I feel that everything in the world is superfluous.

What I find most unbearable is music. That kind of disturbing

Page 26

the sound of a still heart, should belong to one of the sins in the world.

X X X

I am indifferent to any event, unable to muster a trace of interest, sitting quietly and meditating, like a monk in an ancient temple deep in the mountains.

Take two tablets of (Picric acid).

Wanting to write poetry, I get two lines. My stomach problems will forever hinder my poetic inspiration. Lately, it feels like I have woken up from a long dream, denying everything in life. For example, writing poetry, writing novels... are all equally boring and equally meaningless, because this is writing, and it also becomes a burden on the world in the same way.

Heaven has a will. Sitting up at night wrapped in blankets, my mind is blank. Indifferently, I will live like this!

Sailor Street 260

— Zong Xin

Sailor Street, is also in a faraway, nostalgic foreign land. It's a very famous street in the bustling commercial area of Cho Lon in southern Vietnam. It's as long as Nanjing Road in Shanghai!

It's also the place where the most (Chinese) people gather! However, it's absolutely not like the (Chinatowns) in foreign lands that people generally describe, where foreign devils cover their noses as they pass by, showing disgust for the barbaric and filthy Chinese (Chinatowns)!

It's a clean, beautiful, relaxed, and intoxicating street in Southeast Asia! Any overseas Chinese who have been to Cho Lon will want to stroll along Sailor Street, especially Sailor Street at night. I often forget the hateful foreign land from afar; however, the appearance of Sailor Street always floats into my heart. It floats up like the night wind of Southeast Asia! It's strangely nostalgic.

In Shanghai, it's our motherland, and in Southeast Asia, it's undoubtedly a foreign land. But Avenue Joffre in Shanghai is famous like a foreign street. The area around Hongkou Park is even more so, full of exoticism! However, it's difficult to smell even a trace of foreignness on Sailor Street in a foreign land. Don't believe it? It all feels like authentic, local Chinese atmosphere.

It's a place ruled by white people, but you never see a white person! In Cho Lon, on Sailor Street. They don't need to come themselves; they live peacefully in Saigon with very few people. The residents here are so docile. On Sailor Street, you've never seen white sailors as imposing as those in Shanghai; Annamese sailors and Chinese sailors are even more out of the question. So why it's called Sailor Street is not very clear. Now, it's a Sailor Street without sailors.

The relaxed and pleasant twilight is brought by the sea breeze. After being splashed with cold water, feeling light and airy, I love to drift onto Sailor Street. Facing the summer night's cool breeze that permeates my whole body, the thin clothes flutter incessantly, forgetting so many (mundane worries)! Walking, walking, I often walk the very long Sailor Street with a smile against the wind. Unwilling to abandon that relaxed, ethereal, and intoxicating atmosphere, I often tirelessly drift back slowly from the end of the street I just walked, after drinking ice cream. The day's hustle and bustle and dullness are all dissipated on Sailor Street.

The pedestrians are all walking lightly, in front, behind, left, and right, looking, staring intently, they are all Chinese, the same color as myself. It's difficult to recognize many Vietnamese women wearing thin black silk blouses and trousers, their red lips and black teeth chewing betel leaves. There are not many Vietnamese men who are a bit darker than us, just a very small number mixed in that are hard to see. Is this the hometown of the Chinese? I don't have the slightest feeling of being in a foreign land; it's as if I'm not stranded in a foreign land.

I've carefully looked at the doorways of all the shops, big and small, tall and short, and it's hard to find a few shops opened by Annamese people. If there are any, only the old foreign guests would know that some Annamese women are selling cigarettes in small alleys beside shops that are difficult to notice. All other kinds of shops are opened by overseas Chinese. The old foreign guests would sneer at the Vietnamese who are a bit darker than us, calling them stupid pigs, saying they wouldn't know how to do business! It wouldn't work without us Chinese; Southeast Asia was all developed by our overseas Chinese. However, overseas Chinese are gradually declining, and Chinese people are gradually being squeezed out. It was all developed by Chinese overseas; however, in the end, overseas Chinese are being driven out everywhere. I recall the prosperous, beautiful, light, and Chinese-like Sailor Street, and I can't help but repeat it. And I miss it even more: Sailor Street, what are you like now? Will it be much more deserted! The Southeast Asian sea breeze is constantly blowing, mixed with a bit of bloody smell! Overseas Chinese are declining day by day!

Sailor Street, as long and bustling as Nanjing Road in Shanghai, I miss you! In this cold winter in the north, a person whose heart is troubled by life, full of heavy melancholy, when will I be able to lightly float onto Sailor Street again? To blow away my myriad worries!

320 Criminal Cases 261

— San Duo

The Public Works Department Police Department reported on the prison management situation in 1934. On January 1st, there were 6,312 prisoners in the Ward Road Prison. The highest number throughout the year reached 6,357, and the lowest was 6,020.

This is just referring to one prison on Ward Road, and it has already increased threefold compared to the number of prisoners in the same prison in 1925. However, the Third Day Evening News reported that the Municipal Public Security Bureau announced that there were a total of 320 criminal cases in the territory in the past week, with a total of 784 male and female criminals, of which theft cases were the most numerous. Is this number too alarming in just seven days?

The surge in criminals is naturally not a good phenomenon, but the so-called past week is the Lunar New Year, and the most numerous are theft crimes, which shows that the formation of this kind of criminal behavior is somewhat directly affected by the economic situation in the market. It is undeniable that China has suffered from natural and man-made disasters in recent years, and people have no means of livelihood. On the surface of this extravagant and luxurious metropolis, it does indeed make rural people envious as a land of gold, but after reading the above two reports, I worry that the bankruptcy of this metropolis is not necessarily a groundless fear?

In this situation, without seeking fundamental salvation measures for oneself, and continuing to live in a drunken dream with gongs and drums, I am afraid that this number of criminal cases is not the highest record?

Winter on Lighthouse Hill 262

— Yu Renying

Watching a round of rising sun drop below the horizon, the azure blue waves reflecting the sun's pale yellow light. The intense light of the searchlight shines even more brightly, and the signalman dejectedly finishes his shift.

A (golden ring) of a chimney rises from the horizon. Slowly becoming clearer, slowly becoming blurred. Oh, you who live a solitary life on this long journey! Winter on Lighthouse Hill, even more desolate in the melody of the ocean wind. The electric lights in the lighthouse are all bright, and in the darkness, the searchlight's beam dominates the safety of navigators on this coastline in the boundless ocean.

After enduring a night of tedious sitting, I slowly put down the receiver; a companion takes over my work. At night, the seawater beats against the rocks a mile away, echoing in the silence like rhythmic music. The wind blows past the steel-framed walls of the lighthouse, and I lean my head against the gradually yellowing whitewashed wall, flipping through a newspaper from place S a month ago, using the light of sixteen light bulbs.

(Oh, you who live on this desolate island!) I sigh softly, and my mind turns to the "Robinson Crusoe" that I read as a child!

The cigarettes in the cigarette tin are scattered and sparse; this is the last tin left!

(The supply ship) might dock alongside this Lighthouse Hill No. X tomorrow.

(Will it bring news from home?) A wave of melancholy shadows passes through my mind, and I look out the window at the pitch black. The roar of the sea comes in the silence, unable to see the rolling of this azure blue sea, its great posture, submerged in the darkness.

Occasionally, a ray of light reflected from the searchlight shines in from the street railing, and the angry roar of an echo squeezed out of the cinders from a passing ship.

The next day, I stepped into this wireless telegraph room) in the gloomy weather. Seeing the companion's haggard face after a night of exhaustion, the two pieces of living furniture, the buzzer and the receiver, flashed before my eyes, and I squeezed out two tears of a solitary person.

The sea, sweeping past the free flight of seagulls, and the occasional shadow of a few merchant ships, the drifting of a few sailboats at the foot of the mountain. On the desolate island, the outlines of these few skilled companions, the signalman's silent attitude, a life spent drifting on the sea; has aged his brown skin.

(When will I escape this solitary cage?) Watching the glow of the setting sun reflected again on the azure blue water!

On Lighthouse Hill, another winter has passed.

National Studies 265

Sun Deyu Lectures on the Great Learning

Shipping (1180) 7:00 PM to 8:00 PM

The Way of Great Learning lies in illuminating illustrious virtue, in loving the people, and in resting in the highest excellence.

The Great Learning is the learning of great people. Ming means to illuminate. Illustrious virtue is what people receive from Heaven, being vacant and spiritual without obscurity, possessing all principles, and responding to all things. However, being constrained by vital energy and obscured by human desires, there are times when it becomes clouded. However, the luminosity of its essence has never ceased. Therefore, scholars should rely on what is issued and then illuminate it, in order to restore its original state. Xin means to renew the old. It means that after illuminating one's own illustrious virtue, one should also extend it to others, enabling them to remove the stains of their old habits. Zhi means to necessarily arrive at this point and not move from it. Highest excellence is the ultimate of the natural course of affairs and principles. It means that illuminating illustrious virtue and loving the people should all rest in the place of highest excellence and not move from it. It must be that they fully exhaust the ultimate of Heavenly principles, without the slightest selfishness of human desires. These three are the outlines of the Great Learning.
